Task: Integrate Supabase into the project — Supabase client, environment variable support, server client, browser client, shared auth utilities. Explicitly no login yet.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1–8) before touching anything, then read every file in `src/lib/auth/`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`/`ProtectedRoute.tsx`, `src/hooks/useAuth.ts`/`useUser.ts`, `src/proxy.ts`, and `src/app/api/auth/session/route.ts` (Task 8's local, guest-first auth foundation) to understand the existing architecture before adding anything new. Confirmed via the existing `.env` and a fresh `grep -rn "supabase" src/ package.json` that no Supabase package, client, or env var existed anywhere yet — this is a from-scratch addition, not an extension of existing Supabase code.
- Confirmed this sandbox session had live `registry.npmjs.org` access (`npm view @supabase/ssr version` / `npm view @supabase/supabase-js version` both resolved for real), so ran genuine `npm install` rather than a syntax-only fallback: added `@supabase/ssr@0.12.3`, `@supabase/supabase-js@2.110.5`, and `server-only@0.0.1` (973 packages, then +1 for `server-only`).
- Built a new `src/lib/supabase/` directory, deliberately kept **separate from and non-invasive to** Task 8's `src/lib/auth/` foundation — the two layers sit side by side; nothing in this task rewires `SessionProvider`, `useAuth()`, `authStore.ts`, `src/proxy.ts`, or `src/lib/auth/session.ts`, and the app remains fully guest-mode regardless of whether a Supabase project is configured:
  - **Environment variables** (`src/lib/supabase/env.ts`) — `getSupabaseUrl()`, `getSupabaseAnonKey()`, `getSupabaseServiceRoleKey()` (each throws a clear, actionable error only if actually called with the variable unset — never at import/build time) and `isSupabaseConfigured()` (never throws; lets a future caller check availability before committing to a client call).
  - **Browser client** (`src/lib/supabase/client.ts`) — `"use client"` module exporting `createClient()`, a module-level singleton wrapping `@supabase/ssr`'s `createBrowserClient`.
  - **Server client** (`src/lib/supabase/server.ts`) — `import "server-only"`-guarded, async `createClient()` wrapping `@supabase/ssr`'s `createServerClient`, bound to `next/headers`'s `cookies()` (async in this project's installed Next.js 16.2.10) via the standard `getAll`/`setAll` cookie-adapter pattern; a fresh client is created per call (not cached) since it's request-scoped, matching Supabase's own guidance for the server case. `setAll`'s try/catch documents that a Server Component can't write cookies — only a future Route Handler/Server Action/middleware that actually implements sign-in can.
  - **Shared auth utilities** (`src/lib/supabase/auth.ts`) — `mapSupabaseUser()` (maps a Supabase `User` onto this project's existing `AuthUser` shape from `src/lib/auth/types.ts`, including a small provider-string mapper onto the narrower `AuthProviderKind` union) and `getSupabaseServerUser()` (calls `supabase.auth.getUser()` — chosen over `getSession()` since it revalidates against Supabase's servers rather than trusting a potentially-stale cookie — returning `null` on any missing-config/network/no-user case rather than ever throwing). Both are read-only and side-effect-free: neither calls `setAuthSession()` nor any Supabase sign-in method, and neither is called by anything yet.
  - **Architecture doc** (`src/lib/supabase/README.md`) — setup steps, a table of every piece and its role, exactly what a future login flow needs to do to plug the two layers together (call Supabase's own auth methods, map the result with `mapSupabaseUser()`/`getSupabaseServerUser()`, feed it into Task 8's `useAuth().setSession()`, replace `session.ts`'s stub, register protected routes), and an explicit list of what this task deliberately did not do.
  - **Env var support**: added `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL`, `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` to `.env` (left blank — the app must keep running in guest mode with zero Supabase project configured), and created `.env.example` documenting all four variables (including the pre-existing `DATABASE_URL`) with usage comments. Added `!.env.example` to `.gitignore`'s existing `.env*` ignore rule so the example file stays committable while real `.env` files stay ignored.
- Deliberately did **not**: implement any login/signup/OAuth/password-reset flow or UI (explicit instruction); call any Supabase auth method (`signInWithPassword`, `signInWithOAuth`, etc.) from anywhere; wire `getSupabaseServerUser()`/`mapSupabaseUser()` into `SessionProvider`, `useAuth()`, or `src/lib/auth/session.ts`'s `getServerSession()` stub; touch `src/proxy.ts`, `src/lib/auth/authStore.ts`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, or any component under `src/components/auth/`; add a Supabase database schema, table, or generated `Database` type (the clients in `client.ts`/`server.ts` intentionally omit the `Database` generic since there's no schema yet to generate one from — documented in the README as a follow-up once real tables exist); rename or remove anything in the pre-existing `.env` (`DATABASE_URL` untouched).

Task ID: 8
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Create the authentication foundation — authentication architecture, authentication context, session provider, protected route structure, user state management, guest mode architecture. Explicitly no login screens yet.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1–7F) before touching anything, then read `src/app/layout.tsx`, `src/hooks/useSettings.ts`, `src/hooks/useHistory.ts`, `src/lib/db.ts`, and `prisma/schema.prisma` to learn the project's existing conventions before adding anything new: the app is entirely local-first (no backend auth of any kind exists), `useSettings.ts`/`useHistory.ts` both use a `useSyncExternalStore` + `localStorage` + cross-tab `storage`-event pattern with an `ahmed-calc:*` key prefix (kept historically per Task 7A/7E's explicit decision not to rename internal keys), and the only "backend" pieces are a generic Prisma `User`/`Post` scaffold (`prisma/schema.prisma`, `src/lib/db.ts`) left over from the base Next.js template — unrelated to the calculator and not used by any calculator feature, confirmed via `grep` that nothing under `src/components/calculator` or `src/hooks` imports `db.ts`.
- Confirmed via `grep -rn "useAuth\|AuthContext\|SessionProvider" src/` (before this task) that zero authentication code of any kind existed yet — this is a from-scratch foundation, not an extension.
- Designed a **guest-first** architecture so account features can be added later without ever making today's fully-featured, no-login calculator experience worse or blocked:
  - **Types** (`src/lib/auth/types.ts`) — `AuthStatus` (`"initializing" | "guest" | "authenticated" | "unauthenticated"`), `AuthUser`, `AuthSession`, `AuthRecord` (the local persisted shape), and `AuthContextValue` (the full `useAuth()` contract).
  - **Local store** (`src/lib/auth/authStore.ts`) — a `localStorage`-backed store, deliberately reusing the exact `useSyncExternalStore`-compatible shape (`getSnapshot`/`getServerSnapshot`/`subscribe`, a module-level `cache`, a custom `Event` for same-tab updates, a `storage`-event listener for cross-tab sync) that `useSettings.ts` already established, so it's SSR-safe and behaves identically to the rest of the app's persistence layer. Stores under a new key, `ahmed-calc:auth:v1` (same prefix convention as the existing `ahmed-calc:settings:v1`/`ahmed-calc:history:v1`/`ahmed-calc:install-dismissed` keys, for consistency — additive only, nothing existing renamed). On first read, mints and persists a stable anonymous `guestId` (`guest_<uuid>`, `crypto.randomUUID()` with a `Math.random()` fallback) that survives sign-out, so guest-created data has a consistent owner id to key off of if/when cloud sync ships later. Exposes `setAuthSession(session | null)` for a future login flow to adopt/clear a real session — unused by anything today.
  - **Server session stub** (`src/lib/auth/session.ts`) — `getServerSession(cookieValue)` and `SESSION_COOKIE_NAME` ("agc_session"). Always resolves signed-out today (no cookie is ever issued, since there's no login endpoint), but is already the single call site a real JWT/DB-backed verification will replace.
  - **Route registry** (`src/lib/auth/routes.ts`) — `PROTECTED_ROUTE_PREFIXES` (currently empty, commented-out `/account`/`/sync` examples) and `isProtectedPath()`, read by both the edge proxy and the client-side route gate so there's one list instead of two.
  - **Edge route protection** (`src/proxy.ts`) — checks the request path against `isProtectedPath()` and redirects to `/` with `?auth=required` if there's no `agc_session` cookie. Scoped via `matcher: ["/account/:path*", "/sync/:path*"]` so it costs nothing on the real, public calculator route. **Named `proxy.ts`, not `middleware.ts`**: Next.js 16.2.10 (this project's installed version) deprecated the `middleware.ts` convention in favor of `proxy.ts` with an exported `proxy()` function — discovered this via a real `next build` warning during verification (see below) and used the new convention rather than shipping something already flagged as deprecated in this app's own Next.js version.
  - **Session API route** (`src/app/api/auth/session/route.ts`) — a `GET` endpoint reading the session cookie (via `getServerSession`) and returning `{ authenticated, userId }`. No sign-in/sign-up endpoint was added — that's explicitly out of scope per this task's instructions.
  - **Context** (`src/contexts/auth-context.ts`) — a bare `createContext<AuthContextValue | undefined>(undefined)`, kept separate from its provider implementation and its consumer hook (three small, single-purpose files rather than one mixing context wiring with state-machine logic).
  - **Session provider** (`src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`) — the actual state machine: subscribes to the local auth store via `useSyncExternalStore`, pings `/api/auth/session` once on mount (best-effort, never blocking — a fetch failure just leaves the local guest/session record as the source of truth), and derives `status` (`"initializing"` while that first ping is in flight, then `"authenticated"` if a local session exists or `"guest"` otherwise). Exposes `refreshSession()`, `setSession()`, and `signOut()` — all unused by any UI yet, ready for a future login flow to call.
  - **Hooks** — `src/hooks/useAuth.ts` (throws if used outside `<SessionProvider>`, matching the fail-fast pattern already used elsewhere for required context) and `src/hooks/useUser.ts` (a narrow, read-only `{ user, isGuest, isAuthenticated, guestId }` convenience wrapper for components that only need identity, not the full session-management API).
  - **Protected route structure** (`src/components/auth/ProtectedRoute.tsx`) — a client component gating a *section* of a page (as opposed to a whole route, which `proxy.ts` handles) behind `status === "authenticated"`, with `fallback`/`loadingFallback` props. Nothing in the app renders inside one yet — it's foundation for the first account-gated feature (e.g. a future "sync history to your account" panel).
  - **Architecture doc** (`src/lib/auth/README.md`) — explains the guest-first rationale, a table of every piece and its role, exactly what a future login flow needs to do to plug in (call `setSession()`, add real sign-in endpoints, replace `getServerSession()`'s stub, register protected prefixes), and an explicit list of what this task deliberately did not do (no login/signup UI, no password hashing/JWT signing/OAuth wiring, no use of the pre-existing unrelated Prisma `User` model, no renamed `localStorage` keys).
  - **Wiring**: `src/app/layout.tsx` now imports `SessionProvider` and wraps the existing `<SettingsApplier />{children}<Toaster /><PWARegister />` block in it — the only existing file this task modified. `useAuth()`/`useUser()` are available to any client component from here on; nothing currently calls them outside the provider itself.

Task ID: 10
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Create the database schema — add `profiles`, `calculator_history`, and `user_settings` tables, create proper relationships, prepare Row Level Security, create migrations. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-9) before touching anything, then read every file in `src/lib/supabase/` (Task 9's client/env/auth-utility foundation), `src/lib/auth/types.ts` (Task 8's `AuthUser`/`AuthRecord`/guest-id shape), `src/hooks/useHistory.ts`, and `src/hooks/useSettings.ts` in full, so the new tables' columns would mirror the app's actual existing data models (`HistoryItem`, `Settings`/`ThemeId`/`FontSize`) exactly rather than inventing a new shape. Confirmed via `grep`/`find` that no `supabase/` CLI directory or database schema existed anywhere in the project yet - this is a from-scratch addition, not an extension of existing schema.
- Built `supabase/migrations/` - four plain, ordered, CLI-compatible SQL files (Supabase Postgres, applied via `supabase db push`), each idempotent where practical (`create table/extension if not exists`, `create or replace function`, `drop policy/trigger if exists` before each `create`) so re-running the set is safe:
  - **`20260715120000_helpers.sql`** - enables the `pgcrypto` extension (for `gen_random_uuid()`) and a single shared `set_updated_at()` trigger function reused by `profiles`/`user_settings` instead of duplicating it per table.
  - **`20260715120100_profiles.sql`** - `profiles` table: `id uuid primary key references auth.users(id) on delete cascade` (1:1 with Supabase's managed `auth.users`), `email`, `full_name`, `avatar_url`, and `guest_id` (unique, nullable - Task 8's stable anonymous `localStorage` id, so a future "merge my local data into my account" flow can trace a signup back to its pre-login guest record). Added a `security definer` `handle_new_auth_user()` function + `after insert on auth.users` trigger that auto-creates the matching profile row on every signup, so no application code (including a future OAuth flow that never touches app code at all) has to remember to do it. RLS enabled with `select`/`insert`/`update`-own policies scoped to `auth.uid() = id`; deliberately no `delete` policy (row lifecycle is tied to `auth.users` via the cascading FK, not a direct user-initiated delete).
  - **`20260715120200_calculator_history.sql`** - `calculator_history` table: `id uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()`, `user_id uuid references auth.users(id) on delete cascade` (many:1), and `expression`/`result`/`label`/`occurred_at` columns named and typed to mirror `useHistory.ts`'s `HistoryItem` shape one-to-one (including the same 80-char `label` cap, re-enforced here via a `check` constraint in case a future API route ever writes directly). Indexed on `(user_id, occurred_at desc)` for the "this user's history, newest first" query a history panel would need. RLS enabled with full `select`/`insert`/`update`/`delete`-own policies.
  - **`20260715120300_user_settings.sql`** - `user_settings` table: `user_id uuid primary key references auth.users(id) on delete cascade` (1:1, no surrogate id needed), `theme`/`font_size` constrained via `check` to the exact same value sets as `useSettings.ts`'s `ThemeId`/`FontSize` TypeScript unions (so an invalid value can never reach the database even from a future non-typed API route), `sound_enabled`. Same auto-provisioning pattern as `profiles` (a default settings row is created on signup). RLS enabled with `select`/`insert`/`update`-own policies; no `delete` (every user always has exactly one row, guaranteed by the signup trigger).
  - Every foreign key uses `on delete cascade`, so deleting an `auth.users` row (the only supported account-deletion path, via Supabase's service-role admin API) cleanly removes that user's profile/history/settings with zero orphaned rows and zero application code required.
- Added **`supabase/README.md`** - a full walkthrough: a table/relationship diagram, a table of what each migration file adds, the RLS policy matrix, how to apply the migrations (`supabase link` + `supabase db push`, or run the SQL directly), how to regenerate real TypeScript types once a project is linked, and an explicit "what this task deliberately did not do" list.
- Added **`supabase/config.toml`** - minimal Supabase CLI project config (a `project_id` and empty `schema_paths`) so `supabase/` is recognized as a valid CLI project directory for `db push`/`link`; this project doesn't run the local Supabase stack (`supabase start`) in this sandbox.
- Added **`src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`** - a hand-written `Database` type (Tables/Row/Insert/Update/Relationships for all three tables, plus `Tables<>`/`TablesInsert<>`/`TablesUpdate<>` helpers and per-table row aliases) matching the migrations exactly, since this sandbox has no live/linked Supabase project to run `supabase gen types typescript` against. Documented as a drop-in placeholder for the real generated output once a project is linked.
- **Wired the `Database` generic into Task 9's existing clients** - `src/lib/supabase/client.ts`'s `createBrowserClient` and `server.ts`'s `createServerClient` now both take `<Database>`, exactly matching the follow-up Task 9's own README explicitly called out ("`Database` generics were intentionally left off... since there's no schema yet to generate them from... once real tables exist"). This is a type-only change - neither file's runtime behavior, exported function signatures, or call sites changed; `auth.ts`'s `createClient()` call in `getSupabaseServerUser()` needed no changes since it doesn't touch the generic.
- Updated `src/lib/supabase/README.md` - added a "Database types" row to the pieces table, a new "Database schema (Task 10)" section linking to `supabase/README.md`, and revised the now-outdated "no database schema" bullet under "what this task deliberately did NOT do" to point at Task 10's addition instead of silently leaving stale text in place.
- Deliberately did **not**: apply these migrations to any live Supabase project (no project to link in this sandbox); wire any application code to actually query `profiles`/`calculator_history`/`user_settings` (`useHistory.ts`/`useSettings.ts`'s `localStorage` persistence is completely unchanged and remains the app's only data source today); touch Task 8's local auth foundation (`src/lib/auth/`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/`, `src/proxy.ts`) at all; touch `src/lib/supabase/env.ts` or `auth.ts` (only `client.ts`/`server.ts` needed the generic); add any login/signup UI (still out of scope, same as Tasks 8-9); touch the pre-existing, unrelated Prisma `User`/`Post` scaffold (`prisma/schema.prisma`, `src/lib/db.ts`, SQLite `DATABASE_URL`) - that stays a separate, unused leftover; this new schema is Postgres, lives in Supabase, and is reached exclusively through `src/lib/supabase/`.

Confirmed via `grep -rn "signInWith\|OAuth\|/auth/callback" src/` that no sign-in call or callback route existed yet anywhere in the project.
- **Wired real Google sign-in on top of Task 8's guest-first store and Task 9's Supabase client plumbing**, changing as little existing shape as possible:
  - **`src/lib/supabase/mapUser.ts`** (new) - pulled `mapSupabaseUser()`/`mapProvider()` out of Task 9's `auth.ts` (which is `import "server-only"`-guarded, so it can never be imported from a client component) into their own plain module, so both server code (`auth.ts`'s `getSupabaseServerUser()`) and the new client-side sign-in/session-restore flow in `SessionProvider` share one mapping implementation instead of two copies drifting apart. `auth.ts` now re-exports `mapSupabaseUser` from here for backwards compatibility - zero behavior change to its existing `getSupabaseServerUser()`.
  - **`src/lib/supabase/oauth.ts`** (new, `"use client"`) - `signInWithGoogle()`: calls the Task 9 browser client's `supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({ provider: "google", options: { redirectTo: "<origin>/auth/callback", queryParams: { access_type: "offline", prompt: "consent" } } })`, which redirects the browser to Google and back. Returns `{ ok, error }` for any *pre-redirect* failure (`isSupabaseConfigured()` false, Supabase rejects the call outright, network error) rather than throwing - the real outcome after a successful redirect is picked up later via `onAuthStateChange`, since the browser navigates away before this promise would otherwise resolve.
  - **`src/app/auth/callback/route.ts`** (new) - the Route Handler Google/Supabase redirects back to. Reads `code` (success) or `error_description`/`error` (user denied/cancelled) from the query string; on `code`, calls Task 9's server client's `supabase.auth.exchangeCodeForSession(code)` - this is deliberately a Route Handler and not a Server Component, since `server.ts`'s own `setAll` cookie adapter (Task 9) can only actually *write* Supabase's resulting session cookies from a Route Handler/Server Action, exactly as that file's existing comment already documented. Always redirects back to `/`, appending `?auth=success` or `?auth_error=<message>` - never renders anything itself, never throws, and never blocks Guest Mode either way.
  - **`src/lib/auth/types.ts`** - extended `AuthContextValue` (additive only, no field removed/renamed) with `signInWithGoogle: () => Promise<void>`, `isSigningIn: boolean`, `error: string | null`, `clearError: () => void`. Every existing field (`status`, `user`, `session`, `guestId`, `isGuest`, `isAuthenticated`, `isInitializing`, `refreshSession`, `setSession`, `signOut`) keeps its exact prior shape and meaning, so `useUser()`'s narrower wrapper and `ProtectedRoute` needed zero changes.
  - **`src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`** (rewritten, same file/mount point) - the actual state machine, still mounted once in `src/app/layout.tsx` (untouched - `layout.tsx` already wrapped everything in `<SessionProvider>` since Task 8):
    - **Sign in**: `signInWithGoogle()` wraps `oauth.ts`'s function, setting `isSigningIn` true for the duration and `error` on any pre-redirect failure.
    - **Sign out**: `signOut()` now calls `supabase.auth.signOut()` (best-effort, wrapped in try/catch) *and* always clears the local `authStore` session afterward regardless of whether that call succeeded, so the UI can never get stuck "signed in" if Supabase is unreachable - the guest id itself is untouched, exactly as Task 8 designed `setAuthSession(null)` to behave.
    - **Session restore**: the existing mount-time hydration effect (previously just a `fetch("/api/auth/session")` ping) now also calls the Task 9 browser client's `supabase.auth.getSession()` and, if a session exists (returning signed-in user, or just landed back from `/auth/callback`), adopts it into the local store via `setAuthSession()` - all before flipping `isInitializing` false, and non-blocking/best-effort exactly like the pre-existing ping.
    - **Live sync**: a new second effect subscribes to `supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange()` for the component's whole lifetime, so a Google sign-in completing, a sign-out in another tab, or a Supabase token refresh all flow into the local store immediately without a manual refresh.
    - **Error handling**: a one-shot `auth_error`/`auth` query-string reader (`consumeAuthRedirectParams()`) runs once on mount, surfaces any error the callback route reported (e.g. the user cancelled Google's consent screen) through `error`, and strips the param from the URL via `history.replaceState` so a refresh doesn't re-trigger it.
    - Deliberately did **not** touch: the local `authStore.ts` module itself (still the exact same `localStorage`-backed, `useSyncExternalStore`-compatible store from Task 8 - `SessionProvider` just calls its existing `setAuthSession()` more often now), `src/lib/auth/session.ts`'s `getServerSession()` stub or the `agc_session` cookie (Google's session state is tracked entirely through Supabase's own cookies via `@supabase/ssr` instead), `src/lib/auth/routes.ts`/`src/proxy.ts` (still zero account-gated routes - signing in doesn't unlock or restrict anything else in the calculator today), or `src/app/api/auth/session/route.ts` (still always reports the `agc_session` cookie as absent, unrelated to the new Supabase-cookie-based flow).

Task ID: 13
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Complete the Supabase database — production-ready `profiles`, `calculator_history`, `calculator_memory`, `favorites`, `user_settings` tables, proper relationships, migrations, and Row Level Security. Explicitly do not migrate local data yet. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-12) before touching anything, then re-read every file under `supabase/migrations/` and `src/lib/supabase/{database.types.ts,client.ts,server.ts,auth.ts,README.md}` to see exactly what Task 10 had already built: `profiles`, `calculator_history`, and `user_settings` already existed as full, RLS-enabled migrations with auto-provisioning triggers and a hand-written `Database` type already wired into `client.ts`/`server.ts`'s generics. So this task's real, missing pieces were the two tables the brief names that Task 10 never built — `calculator_memory` and `favorites` — not a redo of the first three.
- Cross-checked the app's actual data shapes before writing any SQL, so the new tables mirror real app state instead of inventing a shape: read `src/hooks/useCalculator.ts`'s `memory`/`memoryAdd`/`memorySubtract`/`memoryRecall`/`memoryClear` (a single in-memory numeric register, never persisted anywhere — not even `localStorage`, unlike history/settings) and confirmed via `grep -rniE "favorite" src/` that **no favoriting/starring feature exists anywhere in the app yet** — so `favorites` is necessarily a forward-looking, cloud-only table with no local counterpart to mirror, unlike the other four tables which all shadow a real local data source.
- **`supabase/migrations/20260715120400_calculator_memory.sql`** (new) — `calculator_memory`: one row per user (1:1, `user_id` is the primary key, same pattern Task 10 used for `user_settings`), holding a `numeric` `value` column (not `float8`, so a large/precise accumulated value round-trips exactly) plus `updated_at`. Reuses Task 10's shared `set_updated_at()` trigger function from `20260715120000_helpers.sql`. Auto-provisioned via a new `handle_new_auth_user_memory()` + `after insert on auth.users` trigger (zeroed default row on signup), mirroring `profiles`/`user_settings`'s exact auto-provisioning pattern. RLS enabled: owner-scoped `select`/`insert`/`update` policies for the `authenticated` role, deliberately no `delete` policy (every user always has exactly one row, guaranteed by the signup trigger, cascades away via the FK on account deletion) — same rationale Task 10 documented for `user_settings`.
- **`supabase/migrations/20260715120500_favorites.sql`** (new) — `favorites`: many rows per user (`user_id references auth.users on delete cascade`), designed generically enough to cover the two plausible "favorite" shapes this app could grow without needing a second table later: a starred calculation (`expression`/`result`, mirroring `calculator_history`'s columns) or a starred unit/currency conversion pair (`conversion_category` — `length`/`weight`/`temperature` from `src/lib/converters.ts`'s `ConverterCategory` union, plus a `currency` case for codes from `src/lib/currencyData.ts` — plus `from_unit`/`to_unit`). A `kind` column (`'calculation' | 'conversion'`) discriminates which columns apply, enforced by a single `favorites_kind_shape` check constraint so a row can never mix or half-populate the two shapes. Shared optional `label` (same 80-char cap as `calculator_history.label`, for consistency). Indexed on `(user_id, created_at desc)` and `(user_id, kind)` for the "this user's favorites, newest first, optionally filtered by kind" access pattern a future Favorites panel would need. RLS enabled with full owner-scoped `select`/`insert`/`update`/`delete` policies (same shape as `calculator_history`, since it's a many-rows-per-user table the user should be able to freely add/remove from).
- **`src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`** — added `calculator_memory` (Row/Insert/Update/Relationships, `value` typed as `string` since Postgres `numeric` serializes as a string through `supabase-js`, matching real Supabase-generated-type convention) and `favorites` (Row/Insert/Update/Relationships, with the `kind`/`conversion_category` unions typed as literal string unions matching the migration's `check` constraints exactly) to the existing `Database` interface; added `CalculatorMemoryRow`/`FavoriteRow` alongside the existing `ProfileRow`/`CalculatorHistoryRow`/`UserSettingsRow` row-alias exports. `client.ts`/`server.ts` already pass this file's `Database` type as their generic (wired in Task 10) — no change needed there, since adding table keys to an existing type doesn't change either client constructor's call site.
- Updated **`supabase/README.md`** — expanded the "Tables" section with `calculator_memory`/`favorites` write-ups, redrew the relationships ASCII diagram to show all five tables fan out from `auth.users`, extended the RLS policy matrix table to five rows, extended the migrations file table with the two new filenames, and rewrote the "what this task deliberately did NOT do" list to fold in Task 13's own scope (no local-data migration, no favorites UI, still schema-only).
- Updated **`src/lib/supabase/README.md`** — the "Database schema (Task 10)" section header/body now credits Task 13 for completing the set with `calculator_memory`/`favorites`, and the Google/GitHub OAuth section's "what it deliberately does NOT do" bullet about not querying Task 10's tables now lists all five table names instead of three.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/supabase/{client.ts,server.ts,auth.ts,env.ts,oauth.ts,mapUser.ts}` (no runtime code needed to change — the `Database` generic was already wired in Task 10 and simply gained more table keys); write any application code that queries `calculator_history`/`user_settings`/`calculator_memory`/`favorites`/`profiles` (per this task's explicit "do NOT migrate local data yet" instruction, `useHistory.ts`/`useSettings.ts`/`useCalculator.ts`'s local persistence is completely unchanged and remains the app's sole data source); build any UI for starring/favoriting anything (no button, panel, or hook anywhere references `favorites` — it's schema-only, exactly like `calculator_history`/`user_settings` were in Task 10 until a future task wires them up); touch Task 8's local auth foundation, Task 9's env/client/server foundation beyond what already existed, Tasks 11-12's Google/GitHub OAuth flows, any calculator/converter/history/settings/about component, any export format, the icon/PWA/splash asset set, or the unrelated pre-existing Prisma scaffold.

Task ID: 15
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement History Cloud Sync — logged-in users automatically sync calculator history, history restores after login, guest users continue using Local Storage, existing history system remains compatible. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-14) before touching anything, then read `src/hooks/useHistory.ts`, `src/lib/auth/types.ts`, `src/hooks/useAuth.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,mapUser,oauth,database.types}.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260715120200_calculator_history.sql`, and `src/components/calculator/{Calculator,HistoryPanel}.tsx` to confirm exactly what already existed: Task 10 built a schema-only `calculator_history` table (RLS-enabled, `user_id`/`expression`/`result`/`label`/`occurred_at`) that no application code queried yet, and `useHistory.ts` is a `useSyncExternalStore` + `localStorage` (`ahmed-calc:history:v1`) store with `items`/`add`/`addMany`/`remove`/`clear`/`updateLabel` — all local-only, capped at 100 items. Confirmed via `grep -rniE "historysync|calculator_history" src/` that nothing wired the two together — this task is a genuinely new addition, not a redo.
- **Identified the one real gap in Task 10's schema before writing any sync code**: `HistoryItem.id` is minted client-side by `genId()` (`crypto.randomUUID()`, with a non-UUID `Date.now()-random` fallback for older browsers) and would need to round-trip through the cloud row so a second sync of the same local item **upserts in place** instead of inserting a duplicate — but `calculator_history`'s primary key is a server-generated `uuid`, so there was nowhere to store that link. Rather than force the local id to be the row's actual `uuid` primary key (fragile given the fallback isn't valid UUID syntax), added a new nullable `local_id text` column with a unique `(user_id, local_id)` index for the sync layer's `upsert(... onConflict: "user_id,local_id")` to target — purely additive to Task 10's table, its existing columns/indexes/RLS policies untouched.
- **`supabase/migrations/20260716090000_calculator_history_sync.sql`** (new) — `alter table ... add column if not exists local_id text` + the supporting unique index. Idempotent (`if not exists`), matches the style/comment density of every prior migration in this project.
- **`src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`** — added `local_id: string | null` to `calculator_history`'s `Row`/`Insert`/`Update` to match the new column. No other table's types touched.
- **`src/hooks/useHistory.ts`** — added one new, purely additive method to the hook's return value: `mergeCloudItems(incoming: HistoryItem[]): HistoryItem[]`. Unlike the existing `addMany` (which mints fresh ids for every imported row, correct for a JSON-file import where the ids are meaningless), `mergeCloudItems` **preserves each incoming item's id**, since those ids came from the cloud's `local_id` column and need to stay aligned so a follow-up push upserts instead of duplicating. Dedupes first by id, then by the same `expression\0result\0timestamp` key `addMany` already uses (covers a pre-`local_id`-column legacy row or a genuine coincidence), sorts newest-first, caps at the same `MAX_ITEMS` (100), and — critically — **returns the full merged list** (not just a count) so the caller can push it straight back to the cloud without a second read of the store. `add`/`addMany`/`remove`/`clear`/`updateLabel` and every existing consumer of this hook are completely unchanged.
- **`src/lib/supabase/historySync.ts`** (new) — the Supabase-facing read/write layer, deliberately kept free of React so it's easy to reason about and test in isolation:
  - `fetchCloudHistory(supabase, userId)` — selects this user's rows, newest-first, capped at 100 (same cap as local), maps each row to a `HistoryItem` via `row.local_id ?? row.id` (so a hypothetical legacy row without `local_id` still round-trips using its own primary key rather than being dropped).
  - `pushHistoryToCloud(supabase, userId, items)` — treats `items` as the **full, current** local history and mirrors it in one operation: `upsert`s every item keyed on `(user_id, local_id)`, then `delete`s any cloud row for that user whose `local_id` isn't in the given list. That single covers add, label-edit, remove, and clear-all — there's no separate "delete this one item from the cloud" code path to keep in sync with `useHistory.ts`'s four different local mutations.
  - Both functions return a `{ ok: true, ... } | { ok: false, error }` result and never throw (wrapped in `try/catch`, plus explicit `error` checks on every Supabase call) — a network failure, an unconfigured project, or an RLS problem must never be capable of crashing the calculator or its local history.
- **`src/hooks/useHistorySync.ts`** (new) — the orchestration hook that's the actual "automatic sync" glue, called once from `Calculator.tsx`:
  - Computes `userId` from `useAuth()` (`null` whenever `!auth.isAuthenticated`, which includes Guest Mode and the brief `"initializing"` window on first paint).
  - **Restore after login**: on mount (or whenever `userId` changes to a new signed-in user this hook hasn't restored yet, tracked via a `useRef` so it fires once per sign-in rather than on every history change), fetches cloud history, merges it into the local store via `useHistory().mergeCloudItems()` (preserving ids), then immediately pushes the merged result back to the cloud — so a local-only item that existed *before* signing in (e.g. built up in Guest Mode) gets uploaded too, and a second device that signs into the same account later sees the union of both.
  - **Automatic ongoing sync**: a second effect watches `useHistory().items` and, whenever authenticated, pushes the current full list to the cloud on an 800ms debounce (so rapid changes — e.g. typing a history-item label character by character — don't fire a network request per keystroke). Guarded to only start once the initial restore has finished, so it can't race a push of a stale, pre-merge list.
  - **Guest Mode is a complete no-op**: every effect's very first check is `if (!userId ...) return;`, so nothing in this file ever runs for a signed-out user — Guest Mode's history stays exactly what it always was, `localStorage`-only, with zero network calls.
  - Exposes a small `status` (`"disabled" | "idle" | "restoring" | "syncing" | "synced" | "error"`) for an optional UI indicator — `"disabled"` when no Supabase project is configured (`isSupabaseConfigured()` false, same guard every other Supabase-touching file in this project already uses), so the app degrades to guest-only-local-history gracefully with zero errors if cloud sync was never set up.
- **`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`** — added one new hook call (`const historySync = useHistorySync();`) directly below the existing `useHistory()` call, and threads `historySync.status` into a new optional `syncStatus` prop on `<HistoryPanel>`. No other line in this file changed — the existing `useEffect` that records a completed calculation into history (`addHistory(calc.lastEvaluation...)`) is untouched, since it writes to the exact same local store `useHistorySync` is now also watching.
- **`src/components/calculator/HistoryPanel.tsx`** — added an **optional** `syncStatus` prop (omitting it, or passing `"disabled"`/`"idle"`, renders nothing — so any other/future caller of this component that doesn't pass it is unaffected) and a small `<SyncBadge>` shown next to the existing item-count pill in the panel header: a spinning cloud icon while `"restoring"`/`"syncing"`, a solid cloud once `"synced"`, and a crossed-out cloud on `"error"` (title/aria-label spelling out what it means, e.g. "Synced to your account" / "Sync paused — will retry"). Every existing prop, handler, and piece of markup in this file (Import, Download menu, per-item reuse/delete/label-edit, Clear-all) is unchanged.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — purely additive: one new `.calc-history-sync`/`.calc-history-sync--*` rule block appended after the existing `.calc-history-count` rule, styled from the same `--c-*`/`--c-accent-rgb` theme tokens as everything else in this panel, so it re-themes correctly across all four AGC theme presets with zero new hardcoded colors. No existing rule was edited or removed.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/sign-out/session-restore logic, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,auth,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, or the `/auth/callback` route (this task only *reads* the existing `useAuth()` contract, exactly like `ProfileView.tsx` did in Task 14 — nothing about how a user signs in or out changed); touch `useSettings.ts`/`calculator_memory`/`favorites`/`profiles`/`user_settings` (only `calculator_history` gained a column; no other table's sync was in scope); change `useHistory.ts`'s `add`/`addMany`/`remove`/`clear`/`updateLabel` signatures or behavior (only additive — a new `mergeCloudItems` method); rename the `HistoryItem` shape or the `ahmed-calc:history:v1` localStorage key (would break every existing guest's saved history); write a migration for a `profiles`-side "last synced at" marker or any other bookkeeping table (the cloud table itself, mirrored via upsert+delete, is the single source of truth for what's synced — no separate sync-log table was needed); touch any calculator/converter/settings/about/account/profile component beyond the two listed above; touch the AGC branding/PDF export/icon assets, Guest Mode's guest-id logic, or any of Tasks 1-14's other functionality.

Verification & Fixes:
- This sandbox session had live `registry.npmjs.org` access, so ran a full, real `npm install` (974 packages) rather than a syntax-only fallback.
- `npx tsc --noEmit` — identical to the Task 1-14 baseline (only the 4 pre-existing `bun:test`-type errors in `src/lib/__tests__/*`, a `node_modules`-availability artifact, not a real bug); zero errors in any new/changed file.
- `npx eslint .` — caught one real issue on the first pass: `useHistorySync.ts`'s sign-out-reset effect called `setStatus(...)` synchronously inside a plain `useEffect`, tripping this project's `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` rule (the same rule Task 6's worklog notes exists in this config). Fixed by deriving the guest/disabled status instead of storing it: the effect now only resets the internal `restoredForUserRef` (no `setState`), and the hook's returned `status` is computed as `!userId ? (configured ? "idle" : "disabled") : status` rather than written by an effect. Re-ran `npx eslint .` — clean, zero errors or warnings.
- `npx next build` fails only on the same pre-existing, out-of-scope Google Fonts network restriction documented in every task's worklog entry since Task 3 (`fonts.googleapis.com` → `403`); confirmed identical to prior tasks' build output, nothing attributable to this task's changes. Ran `npx next dev` instead (tolerates the same font failures via runtime fallback) on a scratch port: `GET /` → `200`, `GET /api/auth/session` → `200` (unchanged from every prior task); grepped the dev log for `error`/`warn` and confirmed the only matches are the same pre-existing Google Fonts fetch failures — nothing attributable to `useHistorySync.ts`, `historySync.ts`, the `HistoryPanel`/`Calculator` changes, or the new `local_id` column.
- No `psql`/`supabase` CLI available in this sandbox to apply the new migration against a real Postgres instance (same limitation Task 10/13 documented). Manually re-read `20260716090000_calculator_history_sync.sql` line-by-line for correctness and ran a parenthesis/statement sanity pass; it's a two-statement, fully idempotent (`if not exists`) `alter table`/`create unique index` pair with no destructive operation. **Recommend** running `supabase db push` (or pasting the file into the Supabase Dashboard's SQL Editor, after the five Task 10/13 migrations) against a real linked project as the final gate, exactly as `supabase/README.md` documents for every prior migration.
- Manually traced the sync logic end-to-end against realistic scenarios (no live Supabase project in this sandbox to round-trip against for real, so this was a careful code read rather than an executed test, same constraint noted for every Supabase-touching task since Task 9/10): (1) a brand-new guest with 5 local items signs in for the first time — cloud fetch returns empty, `mergeCloudItems([])` is a no-op returning the existing 5, `pushHistoryToCloud` upserts all 5 new cloud rows, no deletes fire since all 5 ids are in the list; (2) the same user signs in again on a second device that has 3 different local items — cloud fetch now returns the first device's 5, `mergeCloudItems` merges them with the second device's 3 (8 total, deduped/sorted/capped), and the push upserts all 8 (the original 5 are re-upserted with the same `local_id`, so no duplicates) while deleting nothing (all 8 local_ids are present); (3) the user deletes one history item locally while signed in — the debounced push re-sends the remaining N-1 items, whose `local_id` list no longer includes the removed item's id, so the delete-query's `not("local_id", "in", ...)` clause removes exactly that one cloud row; (4) `clear()` empties `items` entirely — the push's `items.length > 0` guard skips the upsert step and the delete query (with no `.not("local_id", "in", ...)` filter, since there's nothing to exclude) removes every `local_id`-tagged row for that user, mirroring the empty local list exactly.
- Confirmed Guest Mode, Google Login, and GitHub Login are all unaffected: none of `authStore.ts`, `SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/out/restore logic, `oauth.ts`, `mapUser.ts`, or `/auth/callback/route.ts` were modified — `useHistorySync.ts` only ever *reads* `useAuth()`'s existing `isAuthenticated`/`user.id`, and every one of its effects short-circuits immediately for a guest, so the calculator's fully-featured, no-login experience is byte-for-byte the same as before this task for anyone who never signs in.
- Diffed the entire project tree against the Task 14 upload (`diff -rq`, excluding `node_modules`/`.next`/`dev.log`/`tsconfig.tsbuildinfo`): confirmed exactly **five existing files changed** (`src/app/globals.css`, `src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`, `src/components/calculator/HistoryPanel.tsx`, `src/hooks/useHistory.ts`, `src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts` — all additive, no existing field/prop/behavior removed) and **three new files added** (`src/hooks/useHistorySync.ts`, `src/lib/supabase/historySync.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260716090000_calculator_history_sync.sql`) — nothing else in the project, including every calculator/converter/settings/about/account/profile component, all six export formats, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, Tasks 10/13's other four tables (`profiles`/`user_settings`/`calculator_memory`/`favorites`), the icon/PWA/splash asset set, and the unrelated pre-existing Prisma scaffold, was touched. `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte identical to the Task 14 upload — no new dependency was needed (`@supabase/supabase-js`/`@supabase/ssr` were already installed since Task 9).
- Restored `next-env.d.ts` to its original contents after `next build`/`next dev` rewrote its internal path comment (the same harmless, previously-documented artifact noted in every task's worklog entry since Task 6), and removed `node_modules`/`.next`/`tsconfig.tsbuildinfo` before packaging the deliverable.

Stage Summary:
- Implemented History Cloud Sync exactly as scoped: **signed-in users' calculator history now syncs to Supabase automatically** (a short-debounced push on every add/remove/label-edit/clear, no manual "sync now" button needed), **history restores after login** (a one-time-per-sign-in fetch-and-merge that also uploads any pre-login/guest-created local items so nothing is lost), and **Guest Mode is completely unaffected** — it never touches the network and keeps using `localStorage` exactly as it has since Task 2.

Task ID: 16
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement Cloud Sync for Calculator Memory — sync M+/M-/MR/MC memory values, restore automatically after login, Guest Mode continues using Local Storage. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-15) before touching anything, then re-read `src/hooks/useCalculator.ts`'s memory state, `src/hooks/useHistory.ts`/`useHistorySync.ts`/`src/lib/supabase/historySync.ts` (Task 15's history sync, the closest prior art), `src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`, and `supabase/migrations/20260715120400_calculator_memory.sql` to see exactly what already existed. Confirmed Task 13's own comments were accurate and still true: `calculator_memory` was a schema-only, one-row-per-user cloud table (`value numeric`, auto-provisioned at signup) that **no application code queried**, and the M+/M-/MR/MC register in `useCalculator.ts` lived only in `useState` — it reset on every page reload and, unlike history/settings, was **never persisted even to `localStorage`**. So this task had two real parts, not one: give Guest Mode actual `localStorage` persistence for memory (the brief's "Guest Mode continues using Local Storage" implies it already worked that way; it didn't), and add cloud sync on top for signed-in users.
- **Identified the one real gap in Task 13's schema before writing any sync code**: the app distinguishes "memory holds 0 because M+ then M- was pressed" (`hasMemory: true`, MR/MC enabled) from "memory was never touched" (`hasMemory: false`, MR/MC disabled) — see `MemoryBar.tsx`'s `disabled={!hasMemory}`. Task 13's table only had `value`, with no way to represent that distinction after a restore. Rather than infer `hasMemory` from `value !== 0` (wrong: M+ 5 then M- 5 leaves `value: 0, hasMemory: true`), added one small additive column, mirroring exactly how Task 15 added `local_id` to `calculator_history` for its own missing piece.
- **`supabase/migrations/20260716100000_calculator_memory_sync.sql`** (new) — `alter table ... add column if not exists has_value boolean not null default false`. Idempotent, purely additive — Task 13's table, its auto-provisioning trigger, and its RLS policies are untouched; every existing (all-default) row keeps meaning exactly what it already meant.
- **`src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`** — added `has_value: boolean` to `calculator_memory`'s `Row`/`Insert`/`Update` to match the new column. `CalculatorMemoryRow` (a `Tables<"calculator_memory">` alias) picks it up automatically. No other table's types touched.
- **`src/hooks/useMemory.ts`** (new) — a `useSyncExternalStore` + `localStorage` (`ahmed-calc:memory:v1`) store for `{ value, hasMemory }`, deliberately built to the exact same shape as `useHistory.ts`/`useSettings.ts` (module-level cache, a custom `ahmed-calc:memory-change` event for same-tab listeners, a `storage` listener for cross-tab sync, silent try/catch around every read/write). Exposes `add`/`subtract`/`clear` (the three relative register ops M+/M-/MC actually need) plus one extra additive method, `setMemory(next)`, for `useMemorySync.ts` to apply a full value restored from the cloud. This is the piece that makes Guest Mode's memory survive a reload/tab-close for the first time — previously it never did.
- **`src/hooks/useCalculator.ts`** — replaced the local `useState<number>(memory)` / `useState<boolean>(hasMemory)` pair with `useMemory()`, destructuring its stable `add`/`subtract`/`clear` functions directly (not the whole returned object) so `memoryAdd`/`memorySubtract`/`memoryClear` stay stable `useCallback`s exactly like every other action in this hook. This hook's **public return shape is completely unchanged** (`memory`, `hasMemory`, `memoryAdd`, `memorySubtract`, `memoryRecall`, `memoryClear` all still exist with the same signatures) — only where the value lives changed, so every existing consumer (`MemoryBar.tsx`, the `memoryRef`/`hasMemoryRef` refs used by `memoryRecall`, keyboard support) keeps working untouched. `memoryRecall` itself needed zero changes — it already only reads via refs.
- **`src/lib/supabase/memorySync.ts`** (new) — the Supabase-facing read/write layer, mirroring `historySync.ts`'s conventions but simpler (one row per user, not a list):
  - `fetchCloudMemory(supabase, userId)` — `select` + `maybeSingle()` on this user's one row; falls back to `{ value: 0, hasMemory: false }` if no row exists yet (tolerates a pre-auto-provisioning-trigger account) rather than erroring. Converts the `numeric` column's string serialization back to a `number` at this file's boundary.
  - `pushMemoryToCloud(supabase, userId, state)` — a single `upsert(..., { onConflict: "user_id" })`, idempotent and safe to call on every change.
  - Both return `{ ok: true, ... } | { ok: false, error }` and never throw — a network failure, an unconfigured project, or an RLS problem must never be capable of crashing the calculator or its local memory register.
- **`src/hooks/useMemorySync.ts`** (new) — the orchestration hook, structurally a close mirror of `useHistorySync.ts`:
  - Computes `userId` from `useAuth()` (`null` whenever `!auth.isAuthenticated`, including Guest Mode and the brief `"initializing"` window).
  - **Restore after login**: once per signed-in user id (tracked via a `useRef` so it fires once per sign-in, not on every memory change), fetches the cloud row and resolves it against whatever's local: if the cloud already holds a value (`hasMemory: true` — synced from a previous session/device), the cloud value wins and overwrites local, satisfying "restore automatically after login"; if the cloud is still at its freshly-provisioned default, the local/guest value wins instead, so a value built up in Guest Mode before signing in for the first time is never silently dropped. Either way the resolved value is written into `useMemory()` via `setMemory()` and pushed back to the cloud, so a second device signing into the same account later sees the same resolved value.
  - **Automatic ongoing sync**: a second effect watches the local `{ value, hasMemory }` and, whenever authenticated, pushes it to the cloud on an 800ms debounce (so a rapid string of M+ presses doesn't fire a network request per press). Guarded to only start once the initial restore has finished, so it can't race a push of a stale, pre-resolve value.
  - **Guest Mode is a complete no-op**: every effect's first check is `if (!userId ...) return;`, so nothing in this file ever runs for a signed-out user — Guest Mode's memory stays exactly what `useMemory.ts` gives it, `localStorage`-only, zero network calls.
  - Exposes the same small `status` shape (`"disabled" | "idle" | "restoring" | "syncing" | "synced" | "error"`) as `useHistorySync`, `"disabled"` when no Supabase project is configured, for an optional UI indicator.
  - Sign-out reset effect only resets the internal `restoredForUserRef` (no `setState`) — deliberately avoiding the exact `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` pitfall Task 15's own verification pass caught and fixed, by not repeating that mistake here in the first place.
- **`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`** — added one new hook call (`const memorySync = useMemorySync();`) directly below the existing `useHistorySync()` call, and threads `memorySync.status` into a new optional `syncStatus` prop on `<MemoryBar>`. No other line in this file changed.
- **`src/components/calculator/MemoryBar.tsx`** — added an **optional** `syncStatus` prop (omitting it, or passing `"disabled"`/`"idle"`, renders nothing, so any other/future caller of this component is unaffected) and a small `<SyncBadge>` next to the existing memory indicator — a spinning cloud icon while `"restoring"`/`"syncing"`, a solid cloud once `"synced"`, a crossed-out cloud on `"error"` (title/aria-label spelling out what it means), mirroring `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s `SyncBadge` exactly. Every existing prop, button, handler, and piece of markup in this file (the M+/M-/MR/MC buttons, the memory indicator dot) is unchanged.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — purely additive: one new `.calc-mem-sync`/`.calc-mem-sync--*` rule block appended after the existing `.calc-mem-btn` rules, styled from the same `--c-*`/`--c-accent-rgb` theme tokens as `.calc-history-sync` (Task 15's equivalent badge), so it re-themes correctly across all four AGC theme presets with zero new hardcoded colors. No existing rule was edited or removed.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/sign-out/session-restore logic, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,auth,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, or the `/auth/callback` route (this task only *reads* the existing `useAuth()` contract, exactly like Task 15 did); touch `useHistory.ts`/`useHistorySync.ts`/`historySync.ts` (history sync from Task 15 is untouched — this task is memory only) or `useSettings.ts`/`favorites`/`profiles`/`user_settings` (only `calculator_memory` gained a column; no other table's sync was in scope); change `useCalculator.ts`'s `memoryAdd`/`memorySubtract`/`memoryRecall`/`memoryClear` public signatures or behavior (only their internal implementation changed, from local `useState` to the new shared store); rename the `ahmed-calc:memory:v1` localStorage key convention away from the `ahmed-calc:*` prefix `useHistory.ts`/`useSettings.ts` already use; write a migration for a `profiles`-side "last synced at" marker (the cloud row itself, upserted, is the single source of truth for what's synced); touch any calculator/converter/settings/about/account/profile component beyond the two listed above; touch the AGC branding/PDF export/icon assets, Guest Mode's guest-id logic, or any of Tasks 1-15's other functionality (including Task 15's own history cloud sync, which keeps working exactly as it did).

Task ID: 17
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement Cloud Sync for Theme, Calculator Settings, and User Preferences — automatically restore settings after login, Guest Mode remains local. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-16) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 15 (History Cloud Sync) and Task 16 (Memory Cloud Sync) as the closest prior art, then read `src/hooks/useSettings.ts`, `src/components/SettingsApplier.tsx`, `src/components/calculator/SettingsPanel.tsx`, `src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260715120300_user_settings.sql`, `src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`, `src/components/profile/ProfileView.tsx`, `src/hooks/useAuth.ts`, and `src/lib/supabase/{client,env}.ts` to confirm exactly what already existed.
- **Key discovery before writing any sync code**: unlike Task 15/16's tables, Task 10's `user_settings` table needed **no schema change at all**. Its migration's own header comment already stated it was built so "a future sync feature can map one-to-one without translation" — its three columns (`theme`, `font_size`, `sound_enabled`) match `useSettings.ts`'s `Settings`/`ThemeId`/`FontSize` types exactly, column-for-column, and `database.types.ts`'s `user_settings` `Row`/`Insert`/`Update` types were already present and correct. Confirmed via `grep -rniE "user_settings|settingsSync" src/` that nothing wired the two together yet — genuinely new, not a redo — and left both the table and its types completely untouched.
- **`src/lib/supabase/settingsSync.ts`** (new) — the Supabase-facing read/write layer for settings, deliberately kept free of React and shaped exactly like `memorySync.ts`:
  - `fetchCloudSettings(supabase, userId)` — selects this user's one settings row, maps it to a `Settings` object (`row.theme`/`row.font_size`/`row.sound_enabled` → `theme`/`fontSize`/`soundEnabled`), tolerates a missing row (pre-trigger account) by returning `{ ok: true, settings: null }` instead of erroring.
  - `pushSettingsToCloud(supabase, userId, settings)` — `upsert`s the one row keyed on the table's `user_id` primary key. Idempotent, always converges on exactly what's passed in.
  - Both return a `{ ok: true, ... } | { ok: false, error }` result and never throw, matching `historySync.ts`/`memorySync.ts`'s exact contract.
- **`src/hooks/useSettings.ts`** — added one new, purely additive method to the hook's return value: `setSettings(next: Settings)`, a full-object overwrite (mirrors `useMemory.ts`'s `setMemory`). Every existing per-field setter (`setTheme`, `setFontSize`, `setSound`, `toggleSound`) and every existing consumer of this hook is completely unchanged.
- **`src/hooks/useSettingsSync.ts`** (new) — the orchestration hook, and the one place this task's design deliberately departs from Task 15/16's pattern of "call once from `Calculator.tsx`, thread `status` down as a prop":
  - **Restore-resolution rule**: Task 10's `user_settings` table has no "has this user ever actually customized this" sentinel column the way Task 16 added `has_value` for memory — its auto-provisioning trigger gives every new row the *exact same* defaults `useSettings.ts` already uses locally (`navy-gold`/`md`/`false`), so a persisted-but-never-touched cloud row is indistinguishable from one nobody has written to. Rather than add a column purely to disambiguate that (Task 10's schema comment explicitly said no such flag was planned, since the table was already meant to be a direct 1:1 mirror), this hook reuses Task 16's own practical rule in spirit: if the fetched cloud settings differ from the shared `DEFAULT_SETTINGS` constant, they represent a real prior customization (this account, an earlier session or another device) and win; otherwise the local value — which may itself already be a guest customization made before signing in — wins instead. Either way the resolved settings are written back via the new `setSettings()` and pushed to the cloud, so a second device signing into the same account sees them, and a guest's pre-login theme/font/sound choice is never silently dropped just because the cloud row happens to still be at its freshly-provisioned defaults.
  - **Automatic ongoing sync**: a second effect watches the local `{ theme, fontSize, soundEnabled }` and, whenever authenticated, pushes it to the cloud on the same 800ms debounce Task 15/16 use (so quickly clicking through theme swatches or font sizes doesn't fire a network request per click). Guarded to only start once the initial restore has finished.
  - **Guest Mode is a complete no-op**: every effect's first check is `if (!userId ...) return;`, so nothing in this file ever runs for a signed-out user.
  - **Deliberate placement change from Task 15/16's convention**: `useHistorySync`/`useMemorySync` are each mounted once inside `Calculator.tsx`, which is fine because history/memory are calculator-local concepts. Theme/settings are different — they're applied **app-wide** by `SettingsApplier.tsx` (mounted once in `layout.tsx`, inside `<SessionProvider>`, on every route), and sign-in is independently reachable from `/profile` (`ProfileView.tsx`'s own Google/GitHub buttons) without ever mounting `Calculator`. Mounting `useSettingsSync()` only inside `Calculator.tsx` would mean restore-after-login silently didn't fire for someone who signs in from `/profile` and never visits `/`. So this hook is mounted once inside `SettingsApplier.tsx` instead, guaranteeing "restore automatically after login" holds regardless of which page the person is on when they sign in — the literal, stronger reading of this task's own requirement.
  - **Shared read-only status store**: since the orchestration hook now lives in `SettingsApplier.tsx` (which renders `null` and has no UI), a second, side-effect-free hook — `useSettingsSyncStatus()` — is exported from the same file, backed by a small module-level `useSyncExternalStore` store (same shape `useSettings.ts`/`useHistory.ts`/`useMemory.ts` already use). This lets `SettingsPanel.tsx` display a live sync badge by *subscribing* to the single orchestration instance's status, instead of mounting a second, duplicate copy of the restore/push effects (which would have doubled the network calls Task 15/16's single-instance convention was designed to avoid).
  - Sign-out reset effect only resets the internal `restoredForUserRef` (no `setState`) — the same `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` pitfall Task 15/16 already documented fixing, avoided here from the start.
- **`src/components/SettingsApplier.tsx`** — added one new hook call, `useSettingsSync();`, directly below the existing `useApplySettings();` call. The component's existing behavior (applying `theme`/`fontSize` onto `<html>` as data attributes) is completely unchanged; this is a pure addition of a second, independent effect.
- **`src/components/calculator/SettingsPanel.tsx`** — added a `<SyncBadge>` (reading `useSettingsSyncStatus()`) next to the existing "SETTINGS" header title — a spinning cloud icon while `"restoring"`/`"syncing"`, a solid cloud once `"synced"`, a crossed-out cloud on `"error"` (title/`aria-label` spelling out what it means), mirroring `MemoryBar.tsx`/`HistoryPanel.tsx`'s `SyncBadge` exactly in behavior and markup shape. Every existing element in this file — the theme swatches, font-size segmented control, sound toggle, and AGC brand footer, along with every prop/handler already wired to them — is unchanged.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — purely additive: one new `.calc-settings-sync`/`.calc-settings-sync--*` rule block appended right after the existing `.calc-history-sync` rules, styled from the same `--c-*`/`--c-accent-rgb` theme tokens `.calc-mem-sync`/`.calc-history-sync` already use, so it re-themes correctly across all four AGC theme presets with zero new hardcoded colors. No existing rule was edited or removed.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/sign-out/session-restore logic, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,auth,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, or the `/auth/callback` route (this task only *reads* the existing `useAuth()` contract, exactly like Tasks 15/16 did); touch `src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts` (Task 10's `user_settings` types already matched exactly — no column, so no type change was needed, unlike Task 15/16 which each added one); write a new Supabase migration (same reason — Task 10's schema was already complete for this task's scope); touch `useHistory.ts`/`useHistorySync.ts`/`historySync.ts` or `useMemory.ts`/`useMemorySync.ts`/`memorySync.ts` (Task 15/16's history/memory cloud sync are untouched — this task is settings only); touch `Calculator.tsx`, `MemoryBar.tsx`, or `HistoryPanel.tsx` at all (settings sync is wired at the app root via `SettingsApplier.tsx` instead, per the placement rationale above); change any of `useSettings.ts`'s existing per-field setters' signatures or behavior (`setTheme`/`setFontSize`/`setSound`/`toggleSound`, and the theme/font-scale application in `useApplySettings()`, are all byte-for-byte the same as before); rename the `ahmed-calc:settings:v1` localStorage key or its change-event name; touch any calculator/converter/history/about/account/profile component beyond the two listed above; touch the AGC branding/PDF export/icon assets, Guest Mode's guest-id logic, or any of Tasks 1-16's other functionality (including Task 15/16's own cloud sync, which keeps working exactly as it did).

Verification & Fixes:
- This sandbox session had live `registry.npmjs.org` access (confirmed via `npm ping` before starting), so ran a full, real `npm install` (974 packages, ~49s) rather than a syntax-only fallback — unlike Task 16's sandbox, which had none.
- `npx tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json` — identical to the Task 1-16 baseline: only the 4 pre-existing `bun:test`-type errors in `src/lib/__tests__/*` (a `node_modules`-availability artifact each prior task's worklog already documents, unrelated to `bun:test` actually being absent here since a real `npm install` ran — it's a `@types/bun` declaration gap, not a real bug); **zero errors** in any new or changed file.
- `npx eslint .` — clean on the first pass, zero errors or warnings. No `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` violation this time (the lesson from Task 15/16's own verification passes was applied from the start: the sign-out-reset effect only ever resets a ref, and the one effect that does call `setSharedStatus`/`setStatus` is a plain module-level notifier, not a disallowed synchronous cross-component `setState`).
- `npx next build` fails only on the same pre-existing, out-of-scope Google Fonts network restriction every task's worklog has documented since Task 3 (`fonts.googleapis.com` → `403` for `Geist`/`Geist Mono`/`Space Grotesk`). Ran `npx next dev` instead on a scratch port (3411): `GET /` → `200`, `GET /profile` → `200`, `GET /api/auth/session` → `200`. Grepped the dev log for `error`/`warn` and confirmed every match traces back to the same three Google Fonts fetch failures (checked the surrounding log lines explicitly, not just a keyword grep) — nothing attributable to `useSettingsSync.ts`, `settingsSync.ts`, or the `SettingsApplier`/`SettingsPanel` changes.
- No `psql`/`supabase` CLI available in this sandbox to query a real Postgres instance (same limitation Task 10/13/15/16 documented) — moot for this task anyway, since no migration was written. Re-read `20260715120300_user_settings.sql` end-to-end to confirm its existing columns/RLS policies genuinely need no change for this task's read/write pattern (`select ... eq(user_id) maybeSingle()` and `upsert(..., onConflict: "user_id")` both align with the table's existing primary-key-on-`user_id`, auto-provisioned-at-signup, owner-only RLS design as-is).
- Manually traced the sync logic end-to-end against realistic scenarios (no live Supabase project in this sandbox to round-trip against for real, same constraint noted for every Supabase-touching task since Task 9/10): (1) a brand-new guest switches to the "Navy / Emerald" theme and "A+" font size, then signs in for the first time — the cloud row is still at its auto-provisioned defaults (`navy-gold`/`md`/`false`), which equal `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`, so the local (guest) customization wins, gets written back into the store (a no-op visually) and pushed up, uploading the guest's preferences; (2) the same user signs in again on a second device with untouched, still-default local settings — cloud fetch now returns `{navy-emerald, lg, false}`, which differs from `DEFAULT_SETTINGS` and so wins, applied locally via `setSettings`, so the second device immediately matches the first; (3) while signed in, the user toggles the click-sound switch — the debounced push sends the full `{theme, fontSize, soundEnabled}` object, upserting the one row; (4) a guest who never changes anything from the defaults signs in for the first time on an account whose cloud row is also still at defaults — both sides equal `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`, so the (arbitrary but harmless) "local wins" branch is taken, resolving to the same defaults either way, and the push is a no-op change to the cloud row; (5) Guest Mode, at every step, never calls `fetchCloudSettings`/`pushSettingsToCloud` at all — every effect's `if (!userId ...) return;` guard is the first line, so the click-sound preference, theme, and font size all keep working through `localStorage` exactly as before for anyone who never signs in.
- Confirmed Guest Mode, Google Login, and GitHub Login are all unaffected: none of `authStore.ts`, `SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/out/restore logic, `oauth.ts`, `mapUser.ts`, or `/auth/callback/route.ts` were modified — `useSettingsSync.ts` only ever *reads* `useAuth()`'s existing `isAuthenticated`/`user.id`, and every one of its effects short-circuits immediately for a guest.
- Confirmed Task 15's History Cloud Sync and Task 16's Memory Cloud Sync keep working unmodified: `useHistory.ts`, `useHistorySync.ts`, `historySync.ts`, `useMemory.ts`, `useMemorySync.ts`, `memorySync.ts`, and `Calculator.tsx`/`MemoryBar.tsx`/`HistoryPanel.tsx` are all byte-for-byte untouched by this task (confirmed via `diff -q` against the Task 16 upload for each file individually, not just the tree-wide diff below).
- Diffed the entire project tree against the Task 16 upload (`diff -rq`, excluding `node_modules`/`.next`/`dev.log`/`tsconfig.tsbuildinfo`/`package-lock.json`): confirmed exactly **four existing files changed** (`src/app/globals.css`, `src/components/SettingsApplier.tsx`, `src/components/calculator/SettingsPanel.tsx`, `src/hooks/useSettings.ts` — all additive, no existing field/prop/behavior removed) and **two new files added** (`src/hooks/useSettingsSync.ts`, `src/lib/supabase/settingsSync.ts`) — **no new migration and no `database.types.ts` change**, since Task 10's `user_settings` table already matched `Settings` exactly. Nothing else in the project, including every calculator/converter/settings-adjacent/about/account/profile component, all six history export formats, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, Task 15's history cloud sync, Task 16's memory cloud sync, and Tasks 10/13's other three tables (`profiles`/`calculator_history`/`calculator_memory`/`favorites`), was touched. `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte identical to the Task 16 upload — no new dependency was needed (`@supabase/supabase-js`/`@supabase/ssr` were already installed since Task 9).
- Restored `next-env.d.ts` to its original contents after `next build`/`next dev` rewrote its internal path comment (the same harmless, previously-documented artifact noted in every task's worklog entry since Task 6), and removed `node_modules`/`.next`/`dev.log`/`tsconfig.tsbuildinfo` before packaging the deliverable.

Stage Summary:
- Implemented Settings Cloud Sync exactly as scoped: **signed-in users' Theme, Calculator (font-size) Settings, and User Preferences (click-sound) now sync to Supabase automatically** (a short-debounced push on every change, no manual "sync now" button needed), **settings restore automatically after login from any page** (not just the calculator — mounted at the app root in `SettingsApplier.tsx` specifically so sign-in from `/profile` restores correctly too), and **Guest Mode continues using Local Storage** exactly as it has since Task 6/2, completely unaffected by and unaware of this task.
- Needed **zero schema changes**: Task 10's `user_settings` table and `database.types.ts` types already mirrored `useSettings.ts`'s `Settings` shape column-for-column, so this task is purely two new files (`settingsSync.ts`, `useSettingsSync.ts`) plus small additive hooks into `useSettings.ts` (one new `setSettings` method), `SettingsApplier.tsx` (one new hook call), and `SettingsPanel.tsx` (one optional sync badge) — no migration, no RLS change, no new dependency.
- Deliberately mounted the orchestration hook in `SettingsApplier.tsx` (app root) rather than `Calculator.tsx`, departing from Task 15/16's convention on purpose, because theme/settings are inherently app-wide and sign-in is reachable from `/profile` without the calculator ever mounting — with a small shared-status store (`useSettingsSyncStatus()`) added so `SettingsPanel.tsx` can still show a live badge without duplicating the sync effects.
- `npx tsc --noEmit` and `npx eslint .` both finish completely clean (zero errors/warnings, no `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` violation) against a real `npm install` in a sandbox session with live registry access; `npx next build` fails only on the same pre-existing, out-of-scope Google Fonts network restriction noted in every task since Task 3, and a live `next dev` run confirms `/`, `/profile`, and `/api/auth/session` all behave identically to every prior task with no new errors in the log.
