Task ID: 18
Agent: main (Z.ai Code orchestrator)
Task: Implement Cloud Sync for Favorites — sync favorites, restore automatically, preserve Local Guest Mode.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-17) before touching anything, then specifically re-read Task 13 (Complete the Supabase database) and Task 15/16/17's history/memory/settings cloud sync entries, since this task's brief ("Sync Favorites") only makes sense read against what those established.
- **Critical scoping finding, confirmed before writing any code**: `grep -rniE "favorite" src/` turned up nothing outside `database.types.ts` — Task 13 built `favorites` as a deliberately schema-only, forward-looking cloud table ("no starring/favoriting UI exists in the app yet," per that migration's own comment and worklog entry). There is no local Favorites feature to layer cloud sync on top of, unlike Tasks 15/16/17 which each had a real `useHistory`/`useCalculator`-memory/`useSettings` local store already in place. So this task necessarily does two things together: (1) build the missing local favorites feature (a starred-calculation shelf, `localStorage`-backed, in the same shape/conventions as `useHistory.ts`) and (2) layer cloud sync on top of it, following Task 15's exact sync convention. Scoped the local feature to **starring a calculation from History** (the "kind = 'calculation'" half of Task 13's `favorites` table) rather than also building conversion-favoriting UI inside `Converter.tsx` — that table's `kind = 'conversion'` half has no UI trigger point that wouldn't mean redesigning the Converter panel, which the brief didn't ask for and which risks the "don't redesign completed UI" instruction. The local store, cloud row shape, and sync layer all still fully support a future `"conversion"` favorite (matching Task 13's table column-for-column) — only the UI trigger for that half is deliberately out of scope.
- **`supabase/migrations/20260716120000_favorites_sync.sql`** (new) — adds one nullable `local_id text` column to Task 13's existing `favorites` table plus a `(user_id, local_id)` unique index, the exact same pattern as Task 15's `20260716090000_calculator_history_sync.sql` migration for `calculator_history`. Purely additive: every existing column, check constraint (`favorites_kind_shape`), index, and RLS policy from Task 13 is untouched.
- **`src/lib/supabase/database.types.ts`** — added `local_id: string | null` (`local_id?: string | null` for Insert/Update) to the `favorites` table's `Row`/`Insert`/`Update` types, mirroring exactly how Task 15 added the same column to `calculator_history`'s types. `CalculatorMemoryRow`/`FavoriteRow`/other row-alias exports are unchanged (still just re-derive from the `Database` interface, which now has one more optional/nullable field).
- **`src/hooks/useFavorites.ts`** (new) — the local favorites store. Byte-for-byte the same `useSyncExternalStore` + localStorage architecture as `useHistory.ts` (SSR-safe cached snapshot, cross-tab sync via a `storage` listener + a same-tab custom event, `MAX_ITEMS` cap at 200), storing under a new, `ahmed-calc:*`-prefixed key (`ahmed-calc:favorites:v1`) so it never collides with `ahmed-calc:history:v1`/`ahmed-calc:settings:v1`/`ahmed-calc:memory:v1`. `FavoriteItem` mirrors Task 13's `favorites` table shape column-for-column (`kind`, nullable `expression`/`result` for a calculation, nullable `conversionCategory`/`fromUnit`/`toUnit` for a future conversion, shared `label`/`timestamp`) rather than reusing `HistoryItem`'s narrower shape, so the cloud sync layer below needs no lossy translation in either direction. Public API: `toggleCalculation(expression, result)` (stars if not already present, un-stars if it is — the single action `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s new star button needs), `isFavoriteCalculation(expression, result)` (selector so the star button/`FavoritesPanel.tsx` can show filled-vs-outline state), `remove`/`clear`/`updateLabel` (same shape as `useHistory.ts`'s), and `mergeCloudItems` (id-preserving merge for cloud restore, same contract as `useHistory.ts`'s own `mergeCloudItems`).
- **`src/lib/supabase/favoritesSync.ts`** (new) — the Supabase read/write layer, structurally identical to `historySync.ts`: `fetchCloudFavorites` (select, newest-first, capped at 200) and `pushFavoritesToCloud` (full-mirror upsert on `(user_id, local_id)` + delete-anything-not-in-the-list), both returning a `{ ok, ... }` result instead of throwing. `rowToFavoriteItem`/the insert-row builder translate every one of Task 13's `favorites` columns (including the `kind`-discriminated calculation/conversion columns) so a future conversion favorite would round-trip correctly even though nothing writes one today.
- **`src/hooks/useFavoritesSync.ts`** (new) — the orchestration hook, structurally identical to `useHistorySync.ts`: no-op for guests/unconfigured Supabase, restore-once-per-signed-in-user-id (fetch → `mergeCloudItems` → push-the-merged-result-back), a short-debounced (800ms) push on every local change while signed in, and a ref-only reset (no `setState`) on sign-out so a future sign-in restores again without the `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` pitfall Task 15/16/17 already documented avoiding.
- **`src/components/calculator/FavoritesPanel.tsx`** (new) — a slide-out panel for browsing/managing starred calculations, deliberately reusing `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s exact shell CSS classes (`calc-history-backdrop`/`calc-history-panel`/`calc-history-header`/`calc-history-close`/`calc-history-actions`/`calc-history-clear`/`calc-history-list`/`calc-history-item`/`calc-history-del`/`calc-history-body`/`calc-history-note`/`calc-history-expr`/`calc-history-result`/`calc-history-empty`/`calc-history-count`) instead of duplicating a second full panel stylesheet — the same reuse pattern `AccountPanel.tsx` already established by sharing `SettingsPanel.tsx`'s `calc-settings-header`/`calc-settings-close`/`calc-settings-body` classes. Only new, favorites-specific CSS is the sync badge (`calc-fav-sync`, see below). Shows: a Star-icon header with item count + `<SyncBadge>` (identical shape/behavior to `HistoryPanel`'s/`MemoryBar`'s/`SettingsPanel`'s), a "Clear all" action with the same tap-twice-to-confirm pattern `HistoryPanel.tsx` uses, an editable note per row (same `calc-history-note` input, capped at 80 chars), click-to-reuse (loads the calculation back into the calculator, same as History's "reuse"), and a per-row remove button. Deliberately does **not** duplicate History's Import/Export UI — favorites are meant to be a small, curated shelf, not something users bulk-import/export, and no export-format concern from Task 3/4 applies to a table Task 13 didn't ask this task to expose that way.
- **`src/components/calculator/HistoryPanel.tsx`** — purely additive: two new optional props, `isFavorite?: (item: HistoryItem) => boolean` and `onToggleFavorite?: (item: HistoryItem) => void` (both must be passed together for the star button to render, so any caller that omits them — none exist today, but the props are optional for safety — sees the exact same row markup as before this task). When both are supplied, each row gets a new star-toggle button (gold-filled once favorited, same fade-in-on-hover/always-visible-on-touch behavior as the existing delete button) to the left of the existing delete button, and the row's `calc-history-body` gets one additional modifier class (`calc-history-body--with-fav`) so its text doesn't run under both buttons. Every existing prop, the import/export flow, the note-editing flow, and the reuse-on-click flow are byte-for-byte unchanged.
- **`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`** — added `useFavorites()`+`useFavoritesSync()` (mirroring the existing `useHistory()`/`useHistorySync()`/`useMemorySync()` calls exactly), one new `favoritesOpen` state, one new toolbar button (a Star icon, placed next to the existing History button) to open `<FavoritesPanel>`, wired the two new optional props into the existing `<HistoryPanel>` element, and rendered `<FavoritesPanel>` alongside the other slide-out panels. `handleReuse` now also closes `favoritesOpen` (in addition to the existing `historyOpen`) since it's the shared "load this calculation back into the display" action for both panels. Every other button, effect, and prop in this file is unchanged.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — purely additive: (1) a new `.calc-fav-sync`/`.calc-fav-sync--*` rule block appended right after the existing `.calc-settings-sync` rules, styled from the same `--c-*`/`--c-accent-rgb` theme tokens `.calc-mem-sync`/`.calc-history-sync`/`.calc-settings-sync` already use, so `FavoritesPanel.tsx`'s sync badge re-themes correctly across all four AGC theme presets with zero new hardcoded colors; (2) `.calc-history-fav`/`.calc-history-fav--active` (the new star-toggle button, shaped like the existing `.calc-history-del` button but positioned 26px further left, gold-filled and always-visible once active) and `.calc-history-body--with-fav` (adds right-padding on rows that show both buttons) appended right after the existing `.calc-history-del` rules. No existing rule was edited, renamed, or removed.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/sign-out/session-restore logic, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,auth,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, or the `/auth/callback` route (this task only *reads* the existing `useAuth()` contract, exactly like Tasks 15/16/17 did); touch `useHistory.ts`/`useHistorySync.ts`/`historySync.ts`, `useCalculator.ts`'s memory methods/`useMemory.ts`/`useMemorySync.ts`/`memorySync.ts`, or `useSettings.ts`/`useSettingsSync.ts`/`settingsSync.ts`/`SettingsApplier.tsx` (Tasks 15/16/17's own cloud sync features are untouched — this task is favorites only, and `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s changes are additive props only, not a rewrite of its own history logic); touch `Converter.tsx`, `CurrencySelect.tsx`, or `src/lib/converters.ts`/`src/lib/currencyData.ts` (no "star a conversion" UI was built, per the scoping rationale above — the local store and cloud schema support it, but no component triggers it yet, so the Converter panel is completely unchanged); rename `HistoryItem`'s shape, the `ahmed-calc:history:v1`/`ahmed-calc:settings:v1`/`ahmed-calc:memory:v1` localStorage keys, or any existing History import/export behavior; write a migration for a `profiles`-side "last synced at" marker (the cloud table itself, mirrored via upsert+delete, is the single source of truth for what's synced, same rationale Task 15 documented); touch any calculator/converter/settings/about/account/profile component beyond the three listed above (`HistoryPanel.tsx`, `Calculator.tsx`, plus the new `FavoritesPanel.tsx`); touch the AGC branding/PDF export/icon assets, Guest Mode's guest-id logic, or any of Tasks 1-17's other functionality.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-18) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 15/16/17/18's four independent cloud-sync features (history, calculator memory, theme/settings, favorites) since this task's brief only makes sense read against what those already built.
- **Key scoping finding, confirmed before writing any code**: there is no missing backend feature here — every piece of user data (`calculator_history`, `calculator_memory`, `user_settings`, `favorites`) already syncs to Supabase automatically via Tasks 15-18's four `use*Sync()` orchestration hooks, each on its own 800ms-debounced push. What's missing is a **person-facing picture of that fact**: nothing anywhere in the app told a signed-in user "yes, your data is being backed up," showed a combined status, or recorded *when* a backup last actually succeeded (each hook's `status` was transient, in-memory-only React state that reset to `"idle"` on every reload). So this task is a read-only aggregation + persistence layer on top of Tasks 15-18, not a new sync pipeline — confirmed via `grep -rniE "backup" src/` returning nothing before this task.
- **`src/lib/backup/backupTimestamps.ts`** (new) — a small, `localStorage`-backed (`ahmed-calc:backup-times:v1`), `useSyncExternalStore` store recording the last successful backup time (epoch ms) for each of the four features independently, following the exact same SSR-safe-cache/cross-tab-`storage`-listener/custom-event conventions `useHistory.ts`/`useMemory.ts`/`useSettings.ts`/`useFavorites.ts` already established. Exposes `recordBackupSuccess(feature)` (called only on a confirmed successful cloud push — never on error/guest/disabled), `useBackupTimestamps()` (read hook), and `latestBackupTime()` (max-of-four helper for the aggregate "Last Backup Time").
- **Wired `recordBackupSuccess()` into all four existing sync hooks, at the exact two points each already transitions to `"synced"`** (the restore-then-push-back path and the ongoing-debounced-push path) — purely additive, one new import + one new call per success point, no existing transition/condition changed:
  - `src/hooks/useHistorySync.ts`, `src/hooks/useMemorySync.ts`, `src/hooks/useFavoritesSync.ts` — each of these three also needed one more small, additive piece: **a shared, read-only status store** (`useHistorySyncStatus()`/`useMemorySyncStatus()`/`useFavoritesSyncStatus()`), so a new aggregation hook could read their live status without mounting a second, duplicate copy of their restore/push effects (which would double the network calls). This is the exact same shared-status pattern Task 17's `useSettingsSync.ts` already established for its own `useSettingsSyncStatus()` — applied here to the three hooks that didn't have it yet. Every existing `setStatus(...)` call site was routed through a new `applyStatus()` wrapper (sets both the local `useState` and the shared store); no existing effect, dependency array, debounce, or guest/disabled-status derivation logic was changed.
  - `src/hooks/useSettingsSync.ts` — already had the shared-status mechanism from Task 17, so only needed the two `recordBackupSuccess("settings")` calls added at its existing success points; nothing else in this file changed.
- **`src/hooks/useCloudBackup.ts`** (new) — the aggregation hook itself, read-only and side-effect-light:
  - Reads all four subsystems' live status via the (now four, one pre-existing + three new) shared `use*SyncStatus()` selectors above — **never** re-invokes `useHistorySync()`/`useMemorySync()`/`useSettingsSync()`/`useFavoritesSync()` themselves, so no duplicate restore/push cycle is ever started by mounting this hook.
  - Reads each of the four local stores (`useHistory()`, `useMemory()`, `useSettings()`, `useFavorites()`) directly — cheap, side-effect-free reads, safe to call again here exactly like every other component in this project already does.
  - Computes an overall `status` (`"disabled"` if no Supabase project; `"guest"` if not signed in; otherwise `"restoring"`/`"syncing"` if any subsystem is actively working, `"error"` if any failed and none are actively working, `"synced"` only once all four report synced, else `"idle"`), an overall `lastBackupAt` (the max of the four recorded timestamps), a per-feature `features[]` breakdown (label + status + individual timestamp), and `automaticBackupEnabled` (simply `configured && signed-in` — there's no separate on/off setting anywhere, since every sync hook already pushes automatically the moment those two things are true; this flag just reports that honestly instead of implying a toggle that doesn't exist).
  - `backupNow()` — a manual "force a push right now" action for signed-in users: directly calls the same four `pushXToCloud()` functions Tasks 15-18's own hooks already use, with the current local state, in parallel via `Promise.all`. Deliberately does **not** duplicate or replace the four hooks' own retry/reconciliation logic — it's an immediate nudge on top of what's already automatic, not a second sync engine; a moment later, re-reading the four shared statuses (already subscribed to) reflects the real per-subsystem outcome.
- **`src/components/profile/CloudBackupSection.tsx`** (new) — the professional UI itself, added to the existing `/profile` page (`ProfileView.tsx`), reusing that page's `calc-settings-section`/`profile-section`/`profile-subsection-label`/`profile-save-btn` primitives rather than inventing a parallel design language:

  - An "Automatic Backup" note line (Zap icon), stating plainly whether it's on right now or will turn on at sign-in — the honest, no-fake-toggle framing described above.
  - A "Last backup time" line (relative formatting: "Just now" / "3 mins ago" / "2 hours ago" / "5 days ago" / falls back to a short date beyond a week — a new small `formatBackupTime()` helper local to this file, same self-contained-formatter convention `ProfileView.tsx`'s own `formatJoinDate()` already uses) plus a detailed per-subsystem list (Calculation history / Calculator memory / Theme & settings / Favorites), each row showing its own icon, its own last-backup time, and a small status word ("Backed up" / "Backing up…" / "Restoring…" / "Paused" / "Waiting").
  - For Guest Mode (or an unconfigured project), the detailed list is replaced with a short, honest explanation of what signing in would enable — never an empty-looking or broken-looking panel.

Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement Manual Backup only — user can manually create a cloud backup, show backup success/failure, do NOT implement restore yet, keep existing export/import working. Return updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-19) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 19's Cloud Backup entry, since it already added a "Back up now" button (`useCloudBackup.ts`'s `backupNow()`) and a Cloud Backup section on `/profile`. Read `src/hooks/useCloudBackup.ts` and `src/components/profile/CloudBackupSection.tsx` end-to-end to confirm exactly what existed before changing anything.
- **Key finding**: Task 19 already built the manual-trigger action (a "Back up now" button calling `backupNow()`, which pushes all four subsystems — history, calculator memory, theme/settings, favorites — to Supabase in parallel) and a status/last-backup-time display. What it explicitly did **not** do — by its own worklog's admission ("Each push helper is intentionally not re-checked for `.ok` here individually... this manual action's job is only to kick off an immediate push") — was give *that specific click* an honest, immediate success/failure answer; it just fired the pushes and let the four automatic sync hooks' own background status eventually catch up, with no direct confirmation and no error surfaced if a push actually failed. This task's brief explicitly asks to "show backup success/failure," so this was the one real gap to close — not a rebuild of the manual-backup feature Task 19 already delivered.
- **`src/hooks/useCloudBackup.ts`**:
  - Added a new exported result type, `ManualBackupResult` (`{ ok: true } | { ok: false; error: string; failedFeatures: BackupFeature[] }`), and changed `backupNow`'s return type from `Promise<void>` to `Promise<ManualBackupResult>`.
  - Rewrote `backupNow`'s body: still fires the same four `push*ToCloud` calls in parallel (byte-identical calls/arguments to Task 19's version), but now actually reads each result's `{ ok, error }` instead of discarding it. If any subsystem's push failed, returns `{ ok: false, error: <first failure's message>, failedFeatures: [...] }` naming exactly which subsystem(s) failed; if all four succeeded, returns `{ ok: true }`. Wrapped the whole body in a `try/catch` so an unexpected thrown error (e.g. `createClient()` itself failing) is also caught and reported as a failure rather than rejecting the promise — the caller always gets a definite answer, never an unhandled rejection. The not-signed-in guard now also returns an explicit `{ ok: false, error, failedFeatures: [] }` instead of returning `undefined`.
  - Every other export, field, and the four automatic sync hooks (`useHistorySync`/`useMemorySync`/`useSettingsSync`/`useFavoritesSync`) this hook reads from are completely untouched — this is purely a return-value change to a single function.
- **`src/components/profile/CloudBackupSection.tsx`**:
  - Added `useToast` (the same toast hook/pattern `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s import flow already uses, `className: "calc-toast"`) and a small local `FEATURE_LABELS` map (human names for the four subsystems, used only to compose a readable failure message).
  - Added `handleBackupNow()`: plays the existing click sound, awaits `backup.backupNow()`, and on success shows a "Backup successful" toast (plus the existing `justBackedUp` checkmark-icon swap on the button, unchanged from Task 19) — on failure, shows a "Backup failed" toast (styled via the existing `destructive` toast variant already defined in `src/components/ui/toast.tsx`) naming which subsystem(s) failed and the underlying error message, and does **not** set `justBackedUp` (so the button doesn't show a false success checkmark).
  - Rewired the existing "Back up now" button's `onClick` to call `handleBackupNow()` instead of firing `backup.backupNow()` directly and optimistically setting `justBackedUp` before knowing the outcome (Task 19's version assumed success up front) — the button's own busy/disabled state, icon, and every other piece of markup are unchanged.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/supabase/{historySync,memorySync,settingsSync,favoritesSync}.ts` (their `{ ok, error }` return contracts were already exactly what `backupNow` needed — no change required there); touch any of the four automatic sync orchestration hooks (`useHistorySync.ts`, `useMemorySync.ts`, `useSettingsSync.ts`, `useFavoritesSync.ts`) or `backupTimestamps.ts` (automatic backup, per-feature status badges, and "Last Backup Time" all keep working exactly as Task 19 built them); implement any restore/pull-from-cloud action or UI (explicitly out of scope per this task's instructions — `backupNow` only ever pushes, never fetches); touch `HistoryPanel.tsx`'s or any other component's Export/Import feature (CSV/XLSX/DOCX/TXT/JSON/PDF export and the JSON Import flow are untouched — confirmed via `grep`/diff that neither file was touched); touch Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, AGC branding, or any of Tasks 1-19's other functionality; add any new dependency (`useToast` was already installed/used elsewhere in the project).

Verification & Fixes:
- This sandbox session had live `registry.npmjs.org` access, so ran a full, real `npm install` (974 packages) rather than a syntax-only fallback.

- src/hooks/useHistory.ts and src/hooks/useFavorites.ts: added a new replaceAll(items) function to each (additive - add/addMany/remove/clear/updateLabel/mergeCloudItems all untouched). Unlike mergeCloudItems (which folds cloud items into whatever's already local, used by the automatic post-login restore), replaceAll overwrites the entire local list outright with what's passed in - sorted newest-first and capped at the same MAX_ITEMS, then written to storage and broadcast via the same emitChange() every other write path already uses. This is the local-store primitive an explicit "restore the backup" action needs that didn't exist before (memory and settings didn't need an equivalent addition - useMemory().setMemory() and useSettings().setSettings() already fully overwrite their single-row state, from Tasks 16/17).
- src/hooks/useCloudBackup.ts:
  - Imported the four fetchCloud* functions alongside the existing push*ToCloud imports.
  - Added ManualRestoreResult ({ ok: true } | { ok: false; error: string; failedFeatures: BackupFeature[] }) - same shape as Task 20's ManualBackupResult, kept as a separate named type since restore and backup are conceptually distinct actions even though their result shape matches.
  - Added restoreBackup(): Promise<ManualRestoreResult> and an isRestoringNow boolean, returned alongside the existing backupNow/isBackingUpNow. restoreBackup mirrors backupNow's structure closely: guards not-signed-in/not-configured the same way, fires all four fetchCloud* calls in parallel via Promise.all, checks each result's .ok individually and reports back exactly which subsystem(s) failed to fetch (never assumes success), and is wrapped in try/catch so a thrown error (e.g. createClient() itself failing) is caught and reported rather than rejecting. Only once all four fetches succeed does it apply anything locally - a partial failure restores nothing, so a person is never left with, say, restored history but stale favorites from a half-applied restore.
  - Applying the fetched data: history.replaceAll(...) and favorites.replaceAll(...) (the new local-store primitive above) for the list-shaped subsystems; memory.setMemory(...) and, when the cloud actually has a settings row (settingsResult.settings is non-null - a brand-new account's row is indistinguishable from "never fetched", so nothing is overwritten in that edge case), settings.setSettings(...) for the two single-row subsystems. This is a deliberate cloud-wins, replace-not-merge action - the person is explicitly restoring a backup, not the passive, additive merge that already happens automatically once per sign-in.
- src/components/profile/CloudBackupSection.tsx:
  - Added a "Restore backup" button next to the existing "Back up now" button (both now sit inside a small new profile-backup-actions flex wrapper so they can sit side by side without breaking the summary row's layout on narrow screens). Only rendered when backup.automaticBackupEnabled - i.e. never shown to Guests, identical gating to "Back up now".
  - Because restoring overwrites local data, added a tap-again-to-confirm interaction on the button - deliberately reusing the exact pattern HistoryPanel.tsx's existing "Clear all" button already established (arm on first click, auto-disarm after 3s, only fire on the second click) rather than introducing a new modal/dialog convention (alert-dialog.tsx exists in src/components/ui but is unused anywhere else in this app and uses default shadcn styling, not this app's navy-gold glass theme - reusing the app's own existing confirm-by-repetition pattern kept the UI/branding consistent instead of adding a visually inconsistent one-off).
  - handleRestoreBackup(): plays the existing click sound, arms/consumes the confirm state, awaits backup.restoreBackup(), and shows a themed "Restore successful" toast on success or a "Restore failed" toast (destructive variant, naming which subsystem(s) failed) on failure - same toast conventions Task 20 already established for backup results.
  - isBusy (which disables both buttons and drives the summary spinner) now also accounts for backup.isRestoringNow, so a restore in flight disables "Back up now" too (and vice versa), preventing the two actions from racing each other.
- src/app/globals.css: added .profile-backup-actions (flex wrapper for the two buttons) and .profile-backup-restore-btn / --confirm (a secondary/outline button styled off the existing .profile-cancel-btn base, with the same rose-tinted confirm state .calc-history-clear--confirm already uses elsewhere) - purely additive; every existing .profile-backup-* rule is unchanged.
- Deliberately did not: touch backup creation in any way - backupNow(), the four automatic debounced push effects, and every push*ToCloud function are byte-for-byte unchanged from Task 20; touch the four fetchCloud* functions themselves (Tasks 15-18 already built exactly the read contract this task needed); touch the automatic restore-after-login merge effects in useHistorySync/useMemorySync/useSettingsSync/useFavoritesSync (still the only thing that runs automatically on sign-in - this task only adds an explicit, user-triggered alternative); touch Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, AGC branding, favicon, PDF exports, or any of Tasks 1-20's other functionality; add any new dependency (lucide-react's Download icon and every hook/component touched were already installed/imported elsewhere in the project); add a new Supabase migration or schema change (the existing five tables and their RLS already support reading a user's own rows, which is all a restore needs).

So the core restore behavior already existed from Tasks 15-18; the question for this task was whether it was actually guaranteed to fire for every "new device / reinstall" scenario, not just some of them.

That's why this gap wasn't visibly breaking anything yet - but it's an accident of today's redirect target and PWA config, not a real guarantee: any future entry point that lands a signed-in session on a page other than `/` (a deep link, a changed redirect, a bookmark straight to /profile with an already-valid session) would silently skip restoring history, calculator memory, and favorites while still restoring settings, since only the settings hook was mounted app-wide. This task closes that gap properly instead of continuing to rely on the redirect coincidence.
- **`src/components/SettingsApplier.tsx`**: mounted useHistorySync(), useMemorySync(), and useFavoritesSync() here too, alongside the existing useSettingsSync() - all four Cloud Sync orchestration hooks now live in the one component that's already mounted once, site-wide, inside `<SessionProvider>` in layout.tsx. Rewrote the file's doc comment to explain why all four now live together here (every subsystem should restore automatically after sign-in "regardless of which page mounts first," not just settings) and noted the side benefit: since this component persists across client-side route navigation (unlike Calculator.tsx, which unmounts/remounts every time a person navigates away from `/` and back), each hook's `restoredForUserRef` now genuinely tracks "has this signed-in session been restored yet" for the whole session, not "has this specific mount of Calculator.tsx been restored yet" - so restore-on-login now fires exactly once per sign-in rather than re-firing (a harmless but wasteful extra fetch+push) every time someone revisits `/`.
- **`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`**: since the actual restore/push effects now live in SettingsApplier.tsx, replaced Calculator.tsx's own useHistorySync()/useMemorySync()/useFavoritesSync() calls (which would otherwise mount a second, duplicate copy of each hook's effects - double the network calls, and a real risk of the two copies' independent debounced pushes racing each other) with the three read-only useHistorySyncStatus()/useMemorySyncStatus()/useFavoritesSyncStatus() selectors those hooks already exported (from Task 19, precisely for this "read status without mounting a second copy" purpose). The three `.status` values Calculator.tsx passes down to MemoryBar/HistoryPanel/FavoritesPanel are unchanged in shape and behavior - only where they're computed changed, not what they show.

- **`src/hooks/useHistorySync.ts`, `useMemorySync.ts`, `useFavoritesSync.ts`, `useSettingsSync.ts`, `useCloudBackup.ts`**: updated doc comments that named the old mount location(s) ("mounted once in Calculator.tsx") to describe the new, single site-wide mount point in SettingsApplier.tsx - comment-only changes in every one of these five files; zero lines of actual logic touched (confirmed by diff - see Verification below).

Task ID: 23
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement Sync Status — display Last Sync, Last Backup, Current Sync State, Sync Progress. Professional AGC UI. Return COMPLETE updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read worklog.md in full (Tasks 1-22) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 19 (built useCloudBackup.ts's aggregation hook and the Cloud Backup section's overall status/last-backup-time display), Task 20/21 (manual Back up now / Restore backup, each with their own success/failure reporting), and Task 22 (moved all four use*Sync() mount points into SettingsApplier.tsx so restore-after-login is guaranteed from every page). Confirmed via grep that no dedicated "Sync Status" display existed yet — Task 19's Cloud Backup section already showed an overall status and a "Last backup time," but not a "Last Sync" figure distinct from backup, and not a numeric/visual "Sync Progress" indicator.
- **Key scoping finding**: "Current Sync State" already existed as useCloudBackup().status (Task 19's CloudBackupStatus, derived from the four subsystems' live statuses) — reused as-is, not recomputed. "Last Backup" also already existed as useCloudBackup().lastBackupAt (Task 19, driven purely by successful cloud pushes recorded via backupTimestamps.ts's recordBackupSuccess()). The two genuinely new pieces were "Last Sync" (a broader figure than "Last Backup": the most recent successful sync activity of any kind, a push or a pull, since Task 21's manual "Restore backup" only ever fetches from the cloud and never updates any of the four per-feature backup timestamps) and "Sync Progress" (no existing figure represented "how many of the four subsystems are currently caught up" as a fraction/bar).
- **`src/lib/backup/syncActivity.ts`** (new) — a small, localStorage-backed (`ahmed-calc:last-sync:v1`), useSyncExternalStore store holding a single "Last Sync" timestamp, following the exact same SSR-safe-cache/cross-tab-storage-listener/custom-event conventions backupTimestamps.ts (Task 19) and every other store in this project already use. Exposes recordSyncActivity() (marks "now" as the last successful sync activity) and useLastSyncAt() (read hook).
- **`src/lib/backup/backupTimestamps.ts`** — one additive change: recordBackupSuccess() (called at all eight existing push-success points across the four sync hooks, unchanged) now also calls recordSyncActivity(), so every successful backup push counts as a sync without touching any of those eight call sites individually. No existing field, function signature, or behavior in this file changed.
- **`src/hooks/useCloudBackup.ts`**:
  - Imported recordSyncActivity/useLastSyncAt from the new syncActivity.ts.
  - Added a new exported CloudSyncProgress type ({ completed, total, percent, active }) and two new fields to UseCloudBackupReturn: lastSyncAt (read from useLastSyncAt()) and progress (derived from the existing features[] array — completed = how many of the four report "synced," active = true while any reports "restoring"/"syncing," percent = completed/total rounded).

Task ID: 24
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement Multi-device Sync — sync user data across devices, handle sync conflicts safely, preserve Guest Mode, do not change existing authentication. Return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-23) before touching anything, with particular attention to Tasks 15-18 (the four independent cloud-sync layers — history, calculator memory, theme/settings, favorites), Task 22 (guaranteed all four restore-after-login from every page via `SettingsApplier.tsx`), and Task 23 (Sync Status UI). Confirmed via a line-by-line read of `useHistorySync.ts`/`useMemorySync.ts`/`useSettingsSync.ts`/`useFavoritesSync.ts` that "sync across devices" already meant two things — an automatic debounced *push* on every local change, and a *restore* that fetches + merges the cloud once per signed-in session (i.e. once per sign-in, not repeatedly) — but nothing anywhere re-checked the cloud again after that first restore while a session stayed open.
- **Key scoping finding, confirmed before writing any code**: this is a real gap, not a hypothetical one — if a person is signed into the same account on two devices at once (a laptop and a phone, say), Device A's push never reaches Device B on its own. B only re-fetches at its *own* next sign-in, so a value changed on A stays invisible on B until B reloads or signs out and back in. That's the concrete behavior this task's "sync user data across devices" and "handle sync conflicts safely" requirements are actually about — not the login-time restore Tasks 15-18/22 already solved, but genuine live reconciliation between two already-open sessions, plus a real answer for what happens when both edit the same piece of data around the same time.
- **`src/lib/supabase/memorySync.ts`** — added `updatedAt: string | null` to `fetchCloudMemory`'s success shape (both the "row exists" and "no row yet" branches). Purely additive: every existing caller (`useMemorySync.ts`, `useCloudBackup.ts`) only ever destructured `.state`, so nothing broke. This column already existed (Task 13's migration, with a `before update` trigger that bumps it to `now()` on every write) but no code read it — it's the one piece this task needed to do real conflict resolution.
- **`src/lib/supabase/settingsSync.ts`** — same additive change to `fetchCloudSettings`'s success shape (`updatedAt: string`, or `null` alongside `settings: null` for a not-yet-provisioned row). Same rationale: Task 10's `user_settings` table already had `updated_at` + its own `before update` trigger; nothing read it before this task.
- **`src/hooks/useMultiDeviceSync.ts`** (new) — the cross-device reconciliation hook, mounted once alongside the other four sync hooks:
  - **Live reconciliation, not just restore-on-login**: while signed in (and only then), periodically (every 20s) re-fetches all four cloud tables and reconciles them into local state — plus immediately on the moments a person is most likely to have just switched from another device: tab becoming visible again, window regaining focus, and the browser coming back online. The very first check is delayed by a full interval specifically so it never races Tasks 15-18's own restore-on-login effects (mounted in the same `SettingsApplier.tsx`, firing immediately on sign-in) — by the time this hook's first check runs, every subsystem has already resolved its initial state.
  - **Conflict resolution — lists (history/favorites)**: reconciled via each store's own existing `mergeCloudItems()` (the same id-preserving, dedupe-by-content union already used for restore-after-login). This can only ever *add* an item neither side already had; it never overwrites or drops a local edit, so a periodic check can't destructively clobber anything no matter how many devices are editing concurrently. If a merge actually added something new, the merged (superset) list is pushed back so a third device converges too — guarded so a merge that added nothing never triggers a needless network push.
  - **Conflict resolution — single-row values (calculator memory/theme settings)**: resolved via **last-write-wins using the cloud row's own `updated_at`** — a Postgres-trigger-maintained, server-clock timestamp, not a client clock (client clocks can drift or be flat-out wrong across two different devices, which would make "which edit is newest" ambiguous or spoofable). Each check compares the freshly-fetched row's `updated_at` against the last one this device has seen; if it's different *and* the row's actual value differs from what's already local, the cloud's value is applied — an unrelated device's own push of the same value, or a fetch that found nothing new, is correctly treated as a no-op rather than a spurious "sync."
  - A failed fetch for any one of the four subsystems doesn't block or skip the other three, and doesn't surface as a user-facing error — it's silently retried on the next tick, matching every other sync hook's own self-healing convention.
  - **Guest Mode is a complete no-op**: every effect's first line is `if (!userId || !configured) return;` — for a guest (or an unconfigured Supabase project) this hook never starts a timer, registers a `visibilitychange`/`focus`/`online` listener, or makes a single network call. A background `setInterval` tick is also skipped whenever `document.hidden` is true, so a signed-in tab left open in the background doesn't spend network calls with no one there to see the result.
  - Exposes the same `useSyncExternalStore`-backed shared-status pattern every other sync hook already uses (`useMultiDeviceSyncStatus()`), plus a small `useLastCrossDeviceCheckAt()` selector, for an optional UI indicator — following it does not start a second, duplicate copy of the polling loop.
  - Sign-out reset effect only clears refs (no `setState`), the same `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` pitfall every prior sync hook's worklog entry already documented avoiding from the start.
- **`src/components/SettingsApplier.tsx`** — added one new hook call, `useMultiDeviceSync();`, directly below the existing four (`useSettingsSync`/`useHistorySync`/`useMemorySync`/`useFavoritesSync`), and extended the file's doc comment to explain why a fifth hook lives here now (same single, app-wide mount point Task 22 established, for the same reason: it must run regardless of which page a signed-in session happens to be on). No existing line in this file changed otherwise.
- **`src/components/profile/SyncStatusSection.tsx`** — added a small, additive "Multi-device sync" note line (reusing this section's existing conventions: a `RefreshCcw` icon, spinning while a check is in flight, and a self-contained relative-time format via the file's own existing `formatTimeAgo()` helper) showing whether this device is actively watching for changes on other devices and when it last checked — shown only when `showLive` is true (the same gate the existing Sync Progress bar already uses), so Guest Mode's screen is completely unchanged. No existing tile, row, or prop in this file was touched.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — purely additive: one new `.profile-sync-live-note` rule appended immediately after the existing `.profile-sync-guest-note` rule, styled from the exact same `--c-text-muted` token, so it re-themes correctly across all four AGC presets with zero new hardcoded colors. No existing rule was edited, renamed, or removed.
- **`supabase/README.md`** — added a new "Multi-device Sync (Task 24)" section (before the existing "What this task... deliberately did NOT do" section) documenting the gap this task closes and, explicitly, the two conflict-resolution rules (union-merge for lists, last-write-wins by server `updated_at` for single-row values) — a permanent record of the actual conflict-safety contract, not just this worklog entry.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch any of the four existing sync hooks' (`useHistorySync`/`useMemorySync`/`useSettingsSync`/`useFavoritesSync`) restore/push/debounce logic, their exported types, or their own shared-status stores (only their two Supabase-layer siblings, `memorySync.ts`/`settingsSync.ts`, gained one additive field each — `historySync.ts`/`favoritesSync.ts` needed no change since their existing `fetchCloud*` functions already return everything `mergeCloudItems`-based reconciliation needs); touch `useHistory.ts`/`useFavorites.ts`/`useMemory.ts`/`useSettings.ts` (their existing `mergeCloudItems`/`setMemory`/`setSettings` primitives already did everything this task needed — no new local-store method was required); touch `useCloudBackup.ts`, `CloudBackupSection.tsx`, `AccountPanel.tsx`, or any calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about component (`Calculator.tsx`, `HistoryPanel.tsx`, `MemoryBar.tsx`, `SettingsPanel.tsx`, `FavoritesPanel.tsx` are all untouched — this task's UI footprint is the one new note line in `SyncStatusSection.tsx`); touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`'s sign-in/sign-out/session logic, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,env,auth,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, or the `/auth/callback` route (this task, like every sync task before it, only ever *reads* `useAuth()`'s existing contract); write a new Supabase migration or add a `database.types.ts` column (both tables' `updated_at` columns and triggers already existed since Tasks 10/13 — this task only started reading a column that was already there); touch the AGC branding/PDF export/favicon assets, Guest Mode's guest-id logic, Google Login, GitHub Login, or any of Tasks 1-23's other functionality; add any new dependency (`RefreshCcw` from `lucide-react` was already imported in this same file).

- Manually traced the new reconciliation logic against realistic multi-device scenarios (no live Supabase project in this sandbox to round-trip a real two-device session against — the same constraint every Supabase-touching task since Task 9 has documented): (1) Device A adds a history item while Device B is open on the same account — on B's next periodic check (or the next time B's tab regains focus), `fetchCloudHistory` returns A's new row, `mergeCloudItems` adds it (A's row wasn't previously in B's local list, so the merge grows and the result is pushed back), and B's calculator now shows it without a reload; (2) Device A presses M+ 5, Device B is still showing 0 — B's next check sees a `calculator_memory` row whose `updated_at` is newer than what B last saw, applies A's `{value: 5, hasMemory: true}` locally since it genuinely differs; (3) both devices happen to poll at nearly the same moment right after A's own push — B's fetch returns the row A itself just wrote, `cloudUpdatedAt` is newer than B's stored marker so B applies it, but since the value already matches what A intended, this converges correctly rather than conflicting (there's only ever one row, so there's no scenario where "whose write wins" is ambiguous — Postgres serializes the writes and `updated_at` reflects whichever commit actually landed last); (4) A stars a calculation as a favorite while B has favorites open — same union-merge as history, B's list grows to include it without erasing anything B had starred locally; (5) a temporary network blip makes one of the four fetches fail during a check — that subsystem's `hadError` flag is set and `status` reports `"error"` for that tick, but the other three subsystems still applied their own results in the same pass, and the next tick 20s later retries cleanly; (6) a guest, or a signed-out session — the interval/listener-registration effect's very first line (`if (!userId || !configured) return;`) means literally zero timers, listeners, or network calls are ever created, confirmed by tracing that no code path in this file executes without a truthy `userId`.

Stage Summary:
- Implemented Multi-device Sync exactly as scoped: **user data now syncs across already-open devices, not just at login** — a new `useMultiDeviceSync()` hook periodically (every 20s, plus immediately on tab-focus/visibility/reconnect) reconciles all four existing cloud subsystems (history, calculator memory, theme/settings, favorites) into local state while signed in, closing the real gap where two simultaneously-open, signed-in devices previously never saw each other's changes without a reload.
- **Sync conflicts are handled safely** with two explicit, documented rules: a non-destructive, id-preserving **union merge** for list data (history/favorites — can only add, never drop or overwrite), and **last-write-wins by the cloud row's own server-clock `updated_at`** for single-row data (calculator memory/theme settings) — trustworthy because it's a Postgres trigger-maintained timestamp, not a client clock that could drift or disagree between two devices.

- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-24) before touching anything. Confirmed via `grep -ri "ai" src/lib` and a full tree listing that no AI-related code, directory, or environment variable existed anywhere in the project yet — this is a brand-new, self-contained subsystem, not an extension of the existing calculator/converter/history/sync/auth features Tasks 1-24 built.
- Studied `src/lib/supabase/env.ts` and `src/lib/supabase/README.md` closely before writing anything, specifically to mirror this project's own established "foundation layer only" conventions: a single `env.ts` module that never throws at import time, an `isXConfigured()` boolean check with no side effects, a `server-only` import guard on anything that could touch a secret, and a `.env`/`.env.example` section left completely blank on purpose with a comment explaining why.
- Built five new files under a new `src/lib/ai/` directory, plus a barrel export and a README:
  - **`env.ts`** — Environment configuration. Reads `AI_PROVIDER`, `AI_MODEL`, `AI_API_KEY`, `AI_BASE_URL` from `process.env` only (`getAIProvider()`, `getAIModel()`, `getAIApiKey()`, `getAIBaseUrl()`), plus `isAIConfigured()` (true only once a real provider name *and* an API key are both present — false for the default, unset case). `import "server-only"` guarded, exactly like `src/lib/supabase/auth.ts`. No default/fallback API key value anywhere; `getAIApiKey()` throws a clear, actionable error if called with nothing set, matching `getSupabaseAnonKey()`'s own `required()` pattern.
  - **`types.ts`** — Shared, provider-agnostic vocabulary: `ChatRole`, `ChatMessage`, `GenerateOptions`, `GenerateRequest`, `GenerateResult`, `AIErrorCode`, and `AIProviderError` (a normalized error class every provider is expected to throw instead of a vendor-specific error shape).
  - **`providerInterface.ts`** — The **Provider Interface** itself: a single `AIProvider` interface (`name` + `generate(request): Promise<GenerateResult>`) any vendor implementation must satisfy. This is the one seam `AIService` depends on.
  - **`providers/noopProvider.ts`** — `NoopProvider`, the only concrete implementation in this task's scope: makes no network call, and its `generate()` throws a typed `AIProviderError("not_configured")` rather than doing nothing silently — "no provider configured" is an explicit, catchable outcome, not a crash or a silent no-op.
  - **`providers/index.ts`** — A small, explicit provider registry (`resolveProvider()`) mapping `AI_PROVIDER`'s value to a factory function; only `"none"` → `NoopProvider` is registered today. Never throws, never returns `undefined` — always resolves to a real `AIProvider`, so a future caller can construct `AIService` freely regardless of configuration state.
  - **`promptManager.ts`** — The **Prompt Manager**: `PromptManager` registers/looks up named `PromptTemplate`s (with `{{variableName}}` placeholder rendering via `render()`), and `buildMessages(templateId, variables, history)` turns a template + variables + a conversation's history into the full ordered `ChatMessage[]` a provider receives (system message first, unmodified history after). `createDefaultPromptManager()` ships with one starting template (`"general-assistant"`) so a future caller doesn't need to hand-register a baseline template at every call site.
  - **`conversationManager.ts`** — The **Conversation Manager**: `ConversationManager` is an in-memory (`Map`-backed), server-process-lifetime store of conversations, with `create`/`get`/`getOrCreate`/`addMessage`/`getHistory` (with optional `maxMessages` trimming)/`clear`/`delete`. Deliberately not persisted to Supabase or anywhere else — this task is architecture-only, with no AI UI or real feature yet needing conversations to survive a server restart; a future task can swap in a persisted-backing implementation behind this same shape.
  - **`aiService.ts`** — The **AI Service Layer**: `AIService` is the single top-level orchestration class, wiring an injected `AIProvider` + `PromptManager` + `ConversationManager` together. Its one real method, `sendMessage()`, records the user's message, builds the prompt via `PromptManager`, calls the resolved provider's `generate()`, records the reply, and returns it — propagating (never swallowing) any `AIProviderError` the provider throws. `getAIService()` returns a shared, lazily-constructed instance wired from `env.ts`/`providers/index.ts`'s `resolveProvider()` and `createDefaultPromptManager()`.
  - **`index.ts`** — a barrel export (`@/lib/ai`) re-exporting every piece above for a future caller.
  - **`README.md`** — documents why this exists, each piece's role in a table (mirroring `src/lib/supabase/README.md`'s own table format), setup steps for a *future* task that adds a real provider, and an explicit "out of scope" list (no AI UI, no API keys, no real provider integration, no persistence, no change to any existing feature).
- **`.env`** / **`.env.example`** — added one new, clearly-labeled "AI Service" section immediately after the existing Supabase section, with `AI_PROVIDER`/`AI_MODEL`/`AI_API_KEY`/`AI_BASE_URL` all left **blank** — no key, no default value, no placeholder secret of any kind — with a comment explaining this is architecture-only (Task 25) and that the app must keep running with nothing configured, exactly mirroring how the existing Supabase section is documented and left blank.
- Deliberately did **not**: add any AI SDK/vendor dependency (`openai`, `@anthropic-ai/sdk`, `ai`/`@ai-sdk/*`, etc.) — `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte unchanged; add any AI-related UI, component, page, or route — no file under `src/app/` or `src/components/` was touched; add or reference any real API key anywhere, including in code, comments, `.env`, or this worklog; touch any existing file outside of the two `.env*` additions above — every calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about/account component, all six history export formats, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, and every one of Tasks 15-24's cloud sync/backup/restore/multi-device-sync features are completely untouched; add a Supabase migration or any persistence for the new `ConversationManager` (explicitly out of scope, called out in the README).

Verification & Fixes:

Task ID: 26
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Prepare AI provider support — create modular providers for OpenAI, Claude, and Gemini, using environment variables. Do NOT connect to providers yet. Return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-25) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 25 (built `src/lib/ai/`'s architecture: `AIProvider` interface, `PromptManager`, `ConversationManager`, `AIService`, `env.ts`, and the single `NoopProvider` registered in `providers/index.ts`). Confirmed Task 25's own README and worklog already anticipated this exact task ("Adding OpenAI/Anthropic/etc. later means adding one more `providers/<vendor>Provider.ts`... and one more entry in this map") — so this task's job was to fill that already-designed seam, not redesign it.
- **Key scoping decision, made before writing any code**: "prepare provider support... do NOT connect yet" means each of the three new provider classes must (a) read real, vendor-specific environment variables, (b) correctly shape a request into that vendor's own wire format (since that's what "modular provider" and "use environment variables" meaningfully require to be true, not just stubbed), but (c) their `generate()` must never call `fetch`, any HTTP client, or any vendor SDK — no exceptions, regardless of whether the environment happens to have real-looking keys in it. Verified this holds by writing a runtime test that constructs each provider with a fake key and confirms `generate()` still always throws rather than ever resolving.
- **`src/lib/ai/types.ts`** — one additive change: added `"not_implemented"` to the existing `AIErrorCode` union, alongside `"not_configured"` (Task 25) and the others — a provider that read a real key/model but was asked to actually generate needs a code distinct from "nothing is configured at all."
- **`src/lib/ai/env.ts`** — added a new `ProviderEnvConfig` shape (`{ apiKey?, model?, baseUrl? }`) and `isProviderConfigComplete()`, plus three new per-vendor config readers — `getOpenAIConfig()` (`OPENAI_API_KEY`/`OPENAI_MODEL`, defaulting to `"gpt-4o-mini"`/`OPENAI_BASE_URL`), `getClaudeConfig()` (`ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`/`ANTHROPIC_MODEL`, defaulting to `"claude-sonnet-4-6"`/`ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL`), `getGeminiConfig()` (`GEMINI_API_KEY`/`GEMINI_MODEL`, defaulting to `"gemini-2.5-flash"`/`GEMINI_BASE_URL`) — and three matching `isOpenAIConfigured()`/`isClaudeConfigured()`/`isGeminiConfigured()` booleans. Each vendor reads its **own** dedicated variables (rather than sharing Task 25's single generic `AI_MODEL`/`AI_API_KEY`/`AI_BASE_URL` trio, which is left completely untouched) specifically so more than one vendor's config can be present in the same environment at once without one overwriting another — "modular" in the environment layer, not just the class layer. Every existing Task 25 export (`getAIProvider`/`getAIModel`/`getAIApiKey`/`getAIBaseUrl`/`isAIConfigured`) is unchanged.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/openaiProvider.ts`** (new) — `OpenAIProvider implements AIProvider`. Reads its config via `getOpenAIConfig()` (injectable via constructor for testing). `isConfigured()` — a public, never-throwing readiness check. `toWireMessages()` — a pure, network-free mapping from this project's `ChatMessage[]` to OpenAI's own `{ role, content }` Chat Completions message shape. `generate()` — throws `AIProviderError("not_configured")` if no key/model, otherwise **always** throws `AIProviderError("not_implemented")` naming the configured model, explicitly stating this task stops short of calling the OpenAI API. No network call, no SDK import, no dependency added.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/claudeProvider.ts`** (new) — `ClaudeProvider implements AIProvider`, same shape as above but reading `getClaudeConfig()` (`ANTHROPIC_*` env vars) and mapping to Anthropic's actual Messages API request shape via `toWireRequest()` — notably pulling any `"system"`-role message(s) out into a separate top-level `system` string (Anthropic's API takes system prompts outside the `messages` array, unlike OpenAI's), since a genuinely correct "modular provider" needs to model that real structural difference, not just relabel OpenAI's shape. Same `"not_configured"`/`"not_implemented"` split, same "no network call" guarantee.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/geminiProvider.ts`** (new) — `GeminiProvider implements AIProvider`, reading `getGeminiConfig()` (`GEMINI_*` env vars) and mapping to Gemini's `generateContent` request shape via `toWireRequest()` — renaming `"assistant"` to Gemini's own `"model"` role, wrapping each message's text in Gemini's `parts` array, and pulling system message(s) into a top-level `systemInstruction`, mirroring that API's real, different-again shape. Same `"not_configured"`/`"not_implemented"` split, same "no network call" guarantee.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/index.ts`** — registered all three new classes in the existing `registry` map (`"openai"` → `OpenAIProvider`, `"claude"` → `ClaudeProvider`, `"gemini"` → `GeminiProvider`), alongside the unchanged `"none"` → `NoopProvider`. `resolveProvider()`'s own logic, signature, and fallback behavior are completely unchanged — it still never throws and never returns `undefined`. Re-exported the three new classes (plus `NoopProvider`) for external use/testing.
- **`src/lib/ai/index.ts`** — added the three new provider classes and the new per-vendor `env.ts` exports (`getOpenAIConfig`/`getClaudeConfig`/`getGeminiConfig`/`isOpenAIConfigured`/`isClaudeConfigured`/`isGeminiConfigured`/`ProviderEnvConfig`) to the barrel, alongside every existing Task 25 export (unchanged).
- **`.env`** / **`.env.example`** — added one new, clearly-labeled section per vendor (OpenAI/Anthropic/Gemini), each with its three variables left **blank** — no key, no default, no placeholder secret — immediately after Task 25's existing generic AI Service section, which itself is completely untouched.
- **`src/lib/ai/README.md`** — updated the intro paragraph, the pieces table (three new rows), and the setup section to describe all three new providers, their env vars, their defaults, and — emphasized explicitly — that none of them make a network call yet; also updated the "explicitly out of scope" list to name the three classes and restate that `generate()` always throws for all of them.
- Deliberately did **not**: make any of the three providers' `generate()` methods call `fetch`, any HTTP client, or any vendor SDK — confirmed by grepping all three new files for `fetch(` and `http` and finding zero matches; add any new npm dependency (`openai`, `@anthropic-ai/sdk`, `@google/generative-ai`, etc.) — `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte unchanged, every new file uses only plain TypeScript and this project's own existing `AIProviderError`/`AIProvider` types; touch `aiService.ts`, `promptManager.ts`, `conversationManager.ts`, or `providerInterface.ts` (Task 25's orchestration layer needed zero changes — the new providers plug into the exact seam Task 25 already built); touch `NoopProvider` or change `"none"`'s behavior in any way; touch Task 25's generic `AI_PROVIDER`/`AI_MODEL`/`AI_API_KEY`/`AI_BASE_URL` env vars or their accessor functions; add any AI UI, component, page, or route; touch any calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about/account component, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, or any of Tasks 1-24's cloud sync/backup/restore/multi-device-sync features.

Task ID: 27
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Create a professional AI Chat interface — Chat Window, Message List, Chat Input, Loading State, and a mobile-responsive layout. Do NOT connect to AI yet. Return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-26) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 25 (built `src/lib/ai/`'s architecture: `AIProvider` interface, `PromptManager`, `ConversationManager`, `AIService`, `env.ts`, `NoopProvider`) and Task 26 (added `OpenAIProvider`/`ClaudeProvider`/`GeminiProvider`, all still non-connecting). Confirmed no AI UI existed anywhere yet (`src/app/`/`src/components/` had no chat-related files).
- **Key scoping decision, made before writing any code**: `src/lib/ai/aiService.ts` is guarded with `import "server-only"`, so it cannot be called directly from a client component — wiring the chat UI into it for real would require adding a server action or API route, which is a connection step this task explicitly excludes ("Do NOT connect to AI yet"). So this task builds a **self-contained, local-only UI**: its own `ChatUIMessage`/`ChatUIRole` types (in `src/components/chat/types.ts`, deliberately separate from `src/lib/ai/types.ts`'s `ChatMessage`/`ChatRole`), with `ChatWindow` owning plain `useState` conversation state. Nothing under `src/components/chat/` imports from `src/lib/ai/`, calls `fetch`, or calls a server action — verified by grep.
- Built a new `src/components/chat/` directory, five new files:
  - **`types.ts`** — `ChatUIRole` (`"user" | "assistant" | "system"`) and `ChatUIMessage` (`id`, `role`, `content`, `createdAt`), documented as UI-local and intentionally not the same type as `src/lib/ai/types.ts`.
  - **`ChatWindow.tsx`** (Chat Window) — the top-level container: header (bot icon, "AI Assistant" title, "Preview — not yet connected" subtitle, a "Clear chat" button), a back link to `/`, and the composed `MessageList` + `ChatInput`. Owns `messages`/`isLoading` state. `handleSend()` appends the user's message, sets `isLoading` true, and after a `setTimeout` (900ms, no network call) appends a `role: "system"` notice — *"This is a preview of the chat interface — AI replies aren't connected yet."* — instead of a fabricated assistant reply, so nothing in the transcript could be mistaken for a real AI response.
  - **`MessageList.tsx`** (Message List) — scrollable transcript (`role="log"`, `aria-live="polite"`), auto-scrolls to the newest message/loading indicator via a ref + `scrollIntoView`, and shows an empty state ("Start a conversation…") before the first message.
  - **`ChatMessageBubble.tsx`** — one row per message: user bubbles (gold, right-aligned, own avatar), assistant bubbles (glass, left-aligned, bot avatar), and system notices (centered, dashed pill, muted) — reusing this project's existing `--c-*` theme tokens throughout instead of any hardcoded color.
  - **`ChatInput.tsx`** (Chat Input) — auto-growing `<textarea>` (grows up to 160px then scrolls), Enter-to-send / Shift+Enter-for-newline, a send button that only activates once there's non-whitespace text and the assistant isn't "typing", 4000-char guard.
  - **`LoadingIndicator.tsx`** (Loading State) — an animated three-dot "typing" bubble (`role="status"`), shown in `MessageList` while `ChatWindow.isLoading` is true; the send button and textarea also disable during this window so a person can't queue a second message mid-"reply".

No other line in this file was touched — every other button, all state, and `ModeTabs`/`Display`/`Keypad`/`Converter`/panel wiring are untouched.

Every rule reuses the existing `--c-*` custom properties (and the existing `.calc-glass`/`.calc-util-btn`/`.profile-back-link`/`.u-divider` classes), so the chat preview re-themes correctly across all four AGC presets (navy-gold / light / navy-emerald / charcoal-rosegold) exactly like every other panel.

A mount-time effect restores any previously saved conversation (validated field-by-field with a small `isStoredMessage` type guard before trusting it, wrapped in `try/catch` for corrupt/inaccessible storage), and a second effect saves on every change, gated behind a `historyLoaded` flag so the initial empty state can never overwrite already-saved history before the restore runs.   - **Copy Response** (new): `ChatMessageBubble.tsx` gained a small copy button (Copy/Check icon swap, 1.8s revert) on every non-user message — assistant-style and system notices alike — mirroring the calculator's own `Display.tsx` copy-to-clipboard pattern exactly (`navigator.clipboard.writeText`, themed `calc-toast` via the existing `useToast` hook, graceful "Copy failed" toasts when the Clipboard API is unavailable or denied). User's own messages don't get a copy button — there's nothing to copy back from something the person just typed.

A small gold "New messages" pill (`chat-scroll-btn`) appears in that case so they can jump back down on their own terms.
