Task ID: 29
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Connect AI Chat to a production-ready provider architecture — use environment variables, no hardcoded API keys, support easy provider switching. Verify the project, update worklog, return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-28) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 25 (built the server-only `src/lib/ai/` architecture — `AIProvider` interface, `PromptManager`, `ConversationManager`, `AIService`, `env.ts`), Task 26 (added `OpenAIProvider`/`ClaudeProvider`/`GeminiProvider`, each reading real per-vendor environment variables and correctly shaping a request into that vendor's own wire format, but every `generate()` deliberately always threw `AIProviderError("not_implemented")` instead of calling the network), and Tasks 27-28 (built the self-contained `src/components/chat/` UI — Chat Window, Message List, Chat Input, Loading State, Conversation History, Copy Response, Clear Chat, Auto Scroll — explicitly **not** connected to `src/lib/ai/` at all; sending a message just replayed a local `setTimeout` "preview" notice).
- **Confirmed the exact gap this task closes**: every architectural piece this task's brief asks for (environment variables, no hardcoded keys, easy provider switching) already existed from Tasks 25-26 — `AI_PROVIDER`'s value already selects a provider via `providers/index.ts`'s registry with zero code change, and every credential was already read from `process.env` only, never hardcoded. What was missing was the actual **connection**: (1) none of the three real providers ever made a network call, and (2) the chat UI never called any of this — it was entirely local-only, by Task 27's own explicit scope. This task wires both up for real, without redesigning either side.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/openaiProvider.ts`** — replaced the always-throwing tail of `generate()` with a real `fetch` call to OpenAI's Chat Completions API (`Authorization: Bearer <apiKey>` header, JSON body built from the existing `toWireMessages()` + `GenerateOptions`). Added `mapOpenAIHttpError()` (401/403 to `authentication_failed`, 429 to `rate_limited`, other 4xx to `invalid_request`, else `provider_error`) and `extractOpenAIContent()`/`extractOpenAIUsage()` to pull the assistant reply and token usage out of OpenAI's response shape. A `fetch` failure itself is caught and re-thrown as `network_error`; a non-JSON or unrecognizable response is `provider_error`. `isConfigured()`, `toWireMessages()`, the constructor, and the `"not_configured"` guard at the top of `generate()` are all unchanged from Task 26.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/claudeProvider.ts`** — same pattern: a real `fetch` call to Anthropic's Messages API (`x-api-key` + `anthropic-version: 2023-06-01` headers), reusing the existing `toWireRequest()` (which already correctly pulls system message(s) into a top-level `system` string) to build the body, plus `max_tokens` (defaulted to 1024 when the caller didn't specify one, since Anthropic's API requires it). Same `mapClaudeHttpError()`/`extractClaudeContent()` (joins Anthropic's `content` array's text blocks)/`extractClaudeUsage()` (`input_tokens`/`output_tokens` mapped to this project's `promptTokens`/`completionTokens`/`totalTokens` shape) treatment.
- **`src/lib/ai/providers/geminiProvider.ts`** — same pattern: a real `fetch` call to Gemini's `generateContent` endpoint, using the `x-goog-api-key` header (rather than putting the key in the URL's `?key=` query string, which risks the key ending up in server access logs) and reusing the existing `toWireRequest()` (already correctly mapping `"assistant"` to `"model"` and pulling system message(s) into `systemInstruction`). Same `mapGeminiHttpError()`/`extractGeminiContent()` (joins the first candidate's `parts[].text`)/`extractGeminiUsage()` treatment.
- Every one of the three providers' HTTP-error mapping, JSON-parse-failure handling, and network-failure handling follows the identical shape on purpose, so `/api/ai/chat` (below) can treat all three uniformly via `AIProviderError.code` regardless of which vendor is configured — exactly the point of `providerInterface.ts`'s seam from Task 25.
- **`src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts`** (new) — the one client-server connection point, and the only new file this task adds. A `POST` handler that: validates the request body (`conversationId`/`message` both required non-empty strings, `message` capped at 8000 chars) with `400` responses for anything malformed; checks `isAIConfigured()` up front and returns `503`/`{ code: "not_configured" }` before ever touching `getAIService()` if nothing is configured; otherwise calls `getAIService().sendMessage({ conversationId, input: message, templateId: "general-assistant", maxHistoryMessages: 20 })` (Task 25's own `AIService`/`ConversationManager`/`PromptManager` orchestration, completely unchanged) and returns `{ reply, provider, conversationId }` on success. On a thrown `AIProviderError`, maps `.code` to the matching HTTP status (`not_configured` to 503, `not_implemented` to 501, `invalid_request` to 400, `authentication_failed` to 401, `rate_limited` to 429, `network_error`/`provider_error` to 502, else 500) and returns `{ error: error.message, code: error.code }` — **deliberately never** including `error.cause` (which may hold a raw vendor HTTP response body) in the JSON sent to the browser; that detail is only ever written to this route's own server-side `console.error`. An unexpected (non-`AIProviderError`) exception is caught separately and reported as a generic `500`/`{ code: "unknown" }` rather than leaking a raw stack trace or error message to the client.
- **`src/components/chat/ChatWindow.tsx`** — replaced `handleSend`'s local `setTimeout` "preview" reply with a real `fetch("/api/ai/chat", ...)` POST. On a non-OK response, the route's own `{ error }` message is shown as a system-role notice (so a `not_configured`/`rate_limited`/`authentication_failed` reply from the route reads as a clear, specific explanation rather than a generic failure); on a network-level `fetch` throw (offline, DNS failure, etc.), a distinct "couldn't reach the AI assistant" notice is shown instead; on success, the returned `reply` becomes a real `role: "assistant"` message — the first one this feature has ever actually produced, as opposed to Task 27/28's hardcoded local notices. Added a stable, `localStorage`-persisted `conversationId` (`agc-ai-chat-conversation-id-v1`, alongside the existing Task 28 history key) — generated once per browser via `crypto.randomUUID()` (with a non-crypto fallback), restored on mount alongside the existing transcript restore, and regenerated whenever "Clear chat" is pressed — so a page reload continues the same server-side `ConversationManager` conversation context instead of starting a fresh, contextless one every visit, while still being a plain opaque id the browser owns (no account/auth tie-in, matching the rest of this feature's local-only identity model). Updated the header subtitle ("Preview — not yet connected" to "AI-powered — replies from your configured provider") and this file's own doc comment to describe the real connection. Every other piece of this file (message restore/persist effects, `MessageList`/`ChatInput` composition, the Clear Chat button's own markup/disabled state, Conversation History's `localStorage` key/shape) is unchanged from Task 28.
- **`.env` / `.env.example`** — no variable was added, removed, or given a default/placeholder value; only the surrounding comments for the existing (still entirely blank) `AI_PROVIDER`/`AI_MODEL`/`AI_API_KEY`/`AI_BASE_URL` and `OPENAI_*`/`ANTHROPIC_*`/`GEMINI_*` sections were updated to say the providers are now connected (rather than "prepared, not connected") and to point at `/api/ai/chat` as the real call site — the actual configuration surface (which variables exist, that every one is left blank, that the app must keep working with nothing set) is byte-for-byte the same shape Task 25/26 established.
- **`src/lib/ai/README.md`** — rewritten to describe the real connection end-to-end: the "Pieces" table's OpenAI/Claude/Gemini rows now describe the real endpoint each one calls and its normalized error mapping instead of "not connected"; added a row for `src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts` itself; the "Setup" section now ends with "restart the dev server and send a message — it now reaches your configured provider for real" instead of "none of the three named providers are connected yet"; added a new "Security notes" section spelling out that no file logs/returns/exposes a key, that error responses never leak `error.cause`, and that every server-only file is still `import "server-only"` guarded so the Next.js build itself would fail if a client component tried to import one directly.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `providerInterface.ts`, `aiService.ts`, `promptManager.ts`, `conversationManager.ts`, `providers/index.ts`, `providers/noopProvider.ts`, or `env.ts` — every seam Task 25/26 already built (the provider registry, the `AIProvider` contract, prompt/conversation management, the per-vendor environment accessors and their defaults) needed zero changes; this task only filled in the three providers' `generate()` bodies and added the one API route that calls into the unchanged orchestration layer. Touch `MessageList.tsx`, `ChatMessageBubble.tsx`, `ChatInput.tsx`, `LoadingIndicator.tsx`, or `src/components/chat/types.ts` (Task 27/28's Message List/Chat Input/Loading Indicator/Copy Response/Auto Scroll are all unchanged — only `ChatWindow.tsx`'s data source changed, not its composition of these components or their own props/behavior). Touch `src/app/chat/page.tsx` or the AI Chat topbar button in `Calculator.tsx` (both already existed and already routed to the chat UI from Task 27 — no new entry point was needed). Add any AI vendor SDK/npm dependency — every provider uses the platform's own `fetch`, matching this project's existing `src/app/api/currency/route.ts` convention of calling external HTTP APIs with plain `fetch` rather than a client library; `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are untouched. Hardcode, default, log, or expose any API key anywhere — every credential is still read from `process.env` only inside `import "server-only"`-guarded files, and the one place a key is ever used (each provider's own outgoing request header) never appears in this task's own responses, log arguments to the browser, or this worklog. Touch `src/lib/auth/*`, `src/lib/supabase/*`, Guest Mode, Google/GitHub Login, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, or any of Tasks 1-24's calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/cloud-sync/backup/restore/multi-device-sync features.

Verification & Fixes:
- This sandbox session had no `node_modules` present (excluded from the delivered archive, as every task's worklog documents) and `bash_tool`'s network egress is disabled in this environment, so a real `npm install`/`next build`/`next dev`/`eslint` round-trip against the live dependency graph wasn't possible here — the same category of constraint several earlier sessions (Tasks 3/4/7A/7C/10/13/16/18/21/22) have documented, though this session's specific limitation (no egress at all, rather than an npm-registry-specific block) is slightly different and is called out plainly rather than glossed over.
- Used the globally-available standalone `typescript` package (v6.0.3) instead: ran `tsc --noEmit --skipLibCheck --strict false --ignoreConfig` (with `--jsx react-jsx --moduleResolution bundler --esModuleInterop`) against every new/changed file individually. Every reported diagnostic across all five files is exactly the same category of environment-only noise every prior network-constrained task's worklog has documented and filtered out (`Cannot find module 'next/server'`/`'@/lib/ai'`/`'react'`, `Cannot find name 'process'`, `react/jsx-runtime` not found, and one `key`-prop false positive on `MessageList.tsx` — a pre-existing, untouched file — all traceable to the missing `node_modules`/`@types/react`/`@types/node`, not to any line this task wrote); zero real syntax or type errors in any of this task's own code.
- Ran an automated parenthesis/brace/bracket-balance check (a small Python script) across all five new/changed files (`openaiProvider.ts`, `claudeProvider.ts`, `geminiProvider.ts`, `route.ts`, `ChatWindow.tsx`) — all balanced.
- Manually re-read every provider's new `generate()` body end-to-end to confirm the discriminated flow is correct: the existing `"not_configured"` guard still fires first and unchanged; the network call is wrapped in its own `try/catch` mapping only a `fetch`-level throw to `"network_error"`; a non-OK HTTP response is mapped via each provider's own `mapXHttpError()` before attempting to parse a body as the success shape; a JSON-parse failure on an OK response is `"provider_error"`; and only once all of that has passed does `extractXContent()` run, itself returning `undefined` (leading to another `"provider_error"`) rather than throwing if the vendor's response shape doesn't contain a recognizable reply — so a malformed/unexpected success response can never silently surface as an empty or `undefined` assistant message reaching the chat UI.
- Manually traced `/api/ai/chat`'s full request lifecycle against several scenarios: (1) `AI_PROVIDER` unset/blank — `isAIConfigured()` is `false`, the route returns `503`/`not_configured` without calling `getAIService()`/any provider at all, and `ChatWindow.tsx` shows that exact message as a system notice; (2) `AI_PROVIDER=openai` with `OPENAI_API_KEY` set but a wrong/revoked key — the real `fetch` reaches OpenAI, gets a `401`, `mapOpenAIHttpError` returns `authentication_failed`, the route responds `401`/that message, the chat UI shows it verbatim (no key or raw response body anywhere in that JSON); (3) a valid key + model — the real request round-trips, `extractOpenAIContent` pulls `choices[0].message.content`, the route returns `{ reply, provider: "openai", conversationId }`, and `ChatWindow.tsx` appends it as a genuine assistant message; (4) switching to `AI_PROVIDER=claude` (or `gemini`) with that vendor's own key set and restarting — `resolveProvider()` (unchanged since Task 26) now builds a `ClaudeProvider`/`GeminiProvider` instead, and every other file in this chain (the route, `ChatWindow.tsx`, `AIService`) needs zero code change to work with the new vendor, confirming "easy provider switching" holds; (5) malformed request body (missing `message`, or a >8000-char message) — `400`/`invalid_request` before any provider/network call is attempted; (6) an unexpected thrown error not wrapped as `AIProviderError` (e.g. a bug elsewhere) — caught by the route's outer `catch`, logged server-side, and reported as a generic `500`/`unknown` rather than leaking a raw stack trace to the browser.
- Confirmed no API key is ever included in any response body this task's code can produce: grepped `route.ts` and all three provider files for every place a caught error's fields are read, and confirmed only `.message`/`.code` (both always plain, human-authored strings — never vendor response bodies) ever reach `NextResponse.json(...)`; `.cause` (which does carry the raw HTTP response text in the HTTP-error path) is only ever passed to `console.error`, never `NextResponse.json`.
- Confirmed Conversation History (Task 28) still works: `ChatWindow.tsx`'s existing `HISTORY_STORAGE_KEY` restore/persist effects, `isStoredMessage` guard, and the localStorage shape of `ChatUIMessage` are all byte-for-byte unchanged — only a second, sibling `localStorage` key (`CONVERSATION_ID_STORAGE_KEY`) was added alongside it, using the same restore-on-mount pattern.
- Confirmed Copy Response, Clear Chat's visual behavior, Auto Scroll, and the Typing Indicator (Tasks 27-28) are all unaffected: `ChatMessageBubble.tsx`, `MessageList.tsx`, `LoadingIndicator.tsx`, and `ChatInput.tsx` are untouched by this task, confirmed via the full-tree diff below; `handleClear` still empties `messages`/clears the persisted transcript (via the existing save-effect's own "remove key when empty" branch, unchanged) and now also regenerates the conversation id, so a cleared chat genuinely starts a fresh conversation on both the client and the server's `ConversationManager` rather than reusing stale server-side context under a "cleared" UI.
- Diffed the entire project tree against the uploaded Task 28 archive (`diff -rq`, excluding `node_modules`/`.next`): confirmed exactly **6 existing files changed** (`.env`, `.env.example` — comment-only, no variable added/removed/defaulted; `src/components/chat/ChatWindow.tsx`; `src/lib/ai/README.md`; `src/lib/ai/providers/openaiProvider.ts`/`claudeProvider.ts`/`geminiProvider.ts`) and **one new file added** (`src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts`). Nothing else in the project — every calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about/account/profile component, all six history export formats, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, every one of Tasks 15-24's cloud sync/backup/restore/multi-device-sync features, Task 25's `providerInterface.ts`/`aiService.ts`/`promptManager.ts`/`conversationManager.ts`/`providers/index.ts`/`providers/noopProvider.ts`/`env.ts`, and Tasks 27-28's `MessageList.tsx`/`ChatMessageBubble.tsx`/`ChatInput.tsx`/`LoadingIndicator.tsx`/`types.ts`/`src/app/chat/page.tsx`/the calculator topbar button — was touched. `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte identical — no new dependency was added (every provider uses the platform's built-in `fetch`; `next/server` was already used by every other API route in this project).

Stage Summary:
- **Connected AI Chat to a production-ready provider architecture** exactly as scoped: the three modular providers Task 26 prepared (`OpenAIProvider`/`ClaudeProvider`/`GeminiProvider`) now make real `fetch` calls to their respective vendor APIs (OpenAI Chat Completions, Anthropic Messages, Gemini `generateContent`), with every HTTP/network/parse failure normalized into a typed `AIProviderError` so the calling code never needs vendor-specific error handling. Task ID: 30
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Implement an AI Calculator integrated with the existing calculator, adding Natural Language Calculations, Formula Explanation, and Step-by-step Solutions — without replacing or modifying the existing calculation logic. Verify the project, update worklog, return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-29) before touching anything, with particular attention to Task 25 (the server-only `src/lib/ai/` architecture — `AIProvider` interface, `PromptManager`, `ConversationManager`, `AIService`, `env.ts`), Task 26 (the three real vendor providers), and Task 29 (the first real connection point, `POST /api/ai/chat`, wiring the pre-existing AI Chat UI to that architecture). Also read `src/lib/nlp.ts` and `src/lib/algebra.ts` closely — this project already has a **rule-based** (non-AI) natural-language parser and equation solver, surfaced through the existing Smart Bar (`SmartBar.tsx`) — so this task's own "Natural Language Calculations" needed to be clearly a distinct, AI-powered feature layered alongside that one, not a rename or a replacement of it.
- **Confirmed the exact shape of this task**: `src/lib/ai/` already provides everything needed (provider-agnostic `AIService`, a `PromptManager` built specifically so "a future 'explain this calculation' feature could register a template" per its own doc comment, and three real, environment-configured providers) — what didn't exist yet was a calculator-specific prompt template, a route that uses it, and a UI surface inside the calculator itself. This task adds exactly those three things and nothing else.
- **The non-negotiable design constraint**: the brief says not to replace or modify the existing calculation logic, so the AI is never trusted for arithmetic. The new route always asks the AI for a **parsed expression** (in this app's own internal expression grammar, spelled out to the model in the system prompt) plus an **explanation** and **steps**, then always computes the real, authoritative number itself by calling `evaluateExpression`/`formatResult` from the completely untouched `src/lib/calculator.ts` — byte-for-byte the same functions the keypad and the existing rule-based Smart Bar already use. If the AI's `expression` can't be evaluated by that engine, the route reports a clear error rather than falling back to a number the AI made up.
- **`src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts`** (new) — the one new client-server seam, following the exact same shape Task 29's `/api/ai/chat/route.ts` established (validate the body, check `isAIConfigured()` up front, call `getAIService()`, map any thrown `AIProviderError` to an HTTP status + `{ error, code }`, never leak `error.cause` to the browser). Registers a new `"ai-calculator-assistant"` prompt template on the shared `PromptManager` the first time it runs (`promptManager.register()` is idempotent/overwrite-safe, and `promptManager.get()` is checked first so repeated requests don't re-register); the template's system prompt spells out the exact expression grammar (`+ - * / ^ ( ) sin() cos() tan() sqrt() log() ln()`, postfix `%`/`!`, constants `pi`/`e`), takes the calculator's current `angleMode` as a `{{angleMode}}` variable, and explicitly instructs the model to respond with strict JSON (`{ expression, explanation, steps }`) and to never assert a specific final numeric answer, since a separate deterministic engine (this route, right after) is the real source of truth for that number. Parses the model's JSON reply (tolerating an accidental ```json fence despite being told not to add one), validates its shape, evaluates `expression` via `evaluateExpression`/`formatResult`, and returns `{ expression, displayExpression, result, explanation, steps, provider }`. Uses a fresh, one-shot `conversationId` per request (this feature asks one question at a time, unlike AI Chat's persisted conversation) and deletes it from `ConversationManager` again in a `finally` block once the reply comes back, so one-shot calculator queries don't accumulate unbounded entries in that in-memory store.
- **`src/components/calculator/AICalculatorPanel.tsx`** (new) — a slide-out panel matching the existing `calc-settings-panel`/`calc-settings-backdrop`/`calc-settings-header`/`calc-settings-body` shell every other panel (`SettingsPanel`, `AboutPanel`, `AccountPanel`, `HistoryPanel`, `FavoritesPanel`) already uses, so it opens/closes/Escape-closes exactly like the rest of the app. Has a textarea + "Ask AI" button (Enter submits, Shift+Enter for a newline), a handful of tappable example questions for first-time discovery, a themed loading state (reusing the same bouncing-dot animation Task 27's chat `LoadingIndicator` already established), a clearly worded error state (including the same `not_configured` message the chat route already returns when nothing is set up), and — once a reply comes back — the engine-computed expression/result, a **Formula explanation** section, a **Step-by-step solution** ordered list, and an **"Insert into calculator"** button. That button calls `calc.loadResult(expression, result)` — the exact same call `SmartBar.tsx`'s existing rule-based natural-language input already makes — so the AI Calculator's result lands in the main display/undo-redo stack exactly the way the existing Smart Bar's own natural-language results already do, with a themed toast confirmation via the existing `useToast` hook.
- **`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`** — added one new `Wand2`-icon topbar button ("AI Calculator") next to the existing Smart Input/AI Chat buttons, one new `aiCalcOpen` state variable, and one new `<AICalculatorPanel open={aiCalcOpen} onClose={...} calc={calc} />` render alongside the other panels. Every other button, state variable, and panel in this file is byte-for-byte unchanged.
- **`src/app/globals.css`** — one new, clearly-labeled, purely additive block appended at the end of the file (`.calc-aic-*` classes for the panel body, input, ask button, example chips, loading dots, error banner, result card, insert button, explanation/steps sections) — every rule reuses this project's existing `--c-*` theme tokens (`--c-accent`, `--c-accent-soft`, `--c-accent-rgb`, `--c-surface-rgb`, `--c-text`, `--c-text-muted`) and the existing `chat-typing-bounce` keyframe, so all four AGC theme presets re-theme it correctly with zero new tokens. Not one existing rule above this new block was touched.
- **`src/lib/ai/README.md`** — updated (not rewritten) to describe the second feature this architecture now backs: a new Pieces-table row for `src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts`, an updated Barrel Export row, and a new "AI Calculator (Task 30)" section explaining the prompt template, the one-shot conversation lifecycle, and — the one point worth repeating in the docs, not just the code — that the AI is never the source of truth for the actual number.
- Deliberately did **not**: touch `src/lib/calculator.ts` (the actual calculation engine — tokenizer, shunting-yard evaluator, `formatResult`, `formatExpressionForDisplay` — is byte-for-byte unchanged; the new route only *calls* its existing exported functions), `src/lib/nlp.ts` or `src/lib/algebra.ts` (the existing rule-based Smart Bar parser/equation solver), `src/components/calculator/SmartBar.tsx` (still calls the same rule-based parser exactly as before — this task adds a second, AI-powered natural-language surface alongside it, not a replacement), `src/lib/ai/providerInterface.ts`, `aiService.ts`, `conversationManager.ts`, `providers/index.ts`, `providers/noopProvider.ts`, `providers/openaiProvider.ts`, `providers/claudeProvider.ts`, `providers/geminiProvider.ts`, or `env.ts` (every seam Tasks 25/26/29 already built needed zero changes — this task only registers one more prompt template on the existing shared `PromptManager` and adds one more route that calls the existing `getAIService()`), `src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts` or any file under `src/components/chat/`/`src/app/chat/` (AI Chat, Task 29's own feature, is completely unaffected), `.env`/`.env.example` (no new environment variable was needed — the AI Calculator reads the exact same `AI_PROVIDER`/vendor-key configuration AI Chat already uses), `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` (no new dependency — the panel uses only the already-installed `lucide-react` icons and the platform's built-in `fetch`), or any calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about/account/profile component, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google/GitHub Login, or any of Tasks 1-24's cloud sync/backup/restore/multi-device-sync features.

Task ID: 31
Agent: main (Z.ai Code orchestrator)
Task: Add a production-ready OCR architecture supporting Image to Text, Receipt Reading, and Math Image Recognition — architecture only, no external OCR API integrated.

Work Log:
- Read this file (Task 1-30 history) before making any change, per this task's own instructions, to understand the project's established patterns — in particular `src/lib/ai/`'s "foundation-layer, provider-interface, safe NoopProvider default" architecture (Task 25) and how `src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts` (Task 30) never trusts an AI-produced value for the actual arithmetic, always re-computing it with `src/lib/calculator.ts`'s own unchanged engine. Built the new OCR architecture as a deliberate structural mirror of that pattern, applied to image recognition instead of chat, and applied the exact same "never trust the recognizer for the number/fields — a separate deterministic/parsing layer always produces the final result" rule to both the Math and Receipt modes.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/types.ts` — provider-agnostic vocabulary: `OCRMode` (`"text" | "receipt" | "math"`), `OCRImageInput`, `OCRRequest`, `OCRRawResult`, `OCRErrorCode`, and a normalized `OCRProviderError` class, mirroring `src/lib/ai/types.ts`'s own shape.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/providerInterface.ts` — the `OCRProvider` contract (`name` + `recognize(request)`) any future vendor implementation must satisfy; the seam `OCRService` codes against instead of any one vendor's SDK.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/env.ts` — `OCR_PROVIDER`/`OCR_MODEL`/`OCR_API_KEY`/`OCR_BASE_URL` accessors and `isOCRConfigured()`, `import "server-only"` guarded, mirroring `src/lib/ai/env.ts`'s structure. Always resolves to "not configured" in this project's shipped state, since every value is left blank in `.env`/`.env.example` and no vendor is registered.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/providers/noopProvider.ts` — `NoopOCRProvider`, the default and, in this task's scope, *only* provider. Makes no network call of any kind; its `recognize()` throws a typed `OCRProviderError("not_configured")`, exactly like `src/lib/ai/providers/noopProvider.ts`'s own role.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/providers/index.ts` — `resolveOCRProvider()`, a registry mapping `OCR_PROVIDER`'s value to a provider factory. Registry has exactly one entry (`"none"` → `NoopOCRProvider`) — deliberately no vendor entry, per this task's explicit "do not integrate external OCR APIs" instruction. Documents, in its own comments, the one-file-plus-one-registry-entry story for adding a real vendor later, without actually adding one.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/imageInput.ts` — `parseImageDataUrl()`, validating and decoding a `data:image/...;base64,...` URL (the same shape `src/hooks/useProfile.ts` already uses for avatar uploads) into `OCRImageInput`, enforcing a PNG/JPEG/WEBP MIME-type allowlist and an ~6 MB decoded-size ceiling (`MAX_IMAGE_BASE64_LENGTH`) before any image reaches a provider, throwing typed `invalid_request`/`unsupported_image_type`/`image_too_large` errors.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/receiptParser.ts` — `parseReceiptText()`, pure/network-free regex-based structuring of raw recognized text into `merchant`/`date`/`items` (description + amount)/`subtotal`/`tax`/`total`/`currency`. Every field is optional and left out (never guessed) when a line doesn't clearly match; handles both `1,234.56` and `1.234,56` amount formats and several date formats.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/mathParser.ts` — `normalizeMathSymbols()`/`extractExpression()`, normalizing OCR/handwriting-flavored symbols (×, ÷, − / – / — dashes, π, √, smart quotes, thousands separators) into this app's own expression grammar (`src/lib/calculator.ts`), picking the most likely candidate line (longest line containing a digit and an operator), and dropping anything from a trailing `=` onward on each line — the recognized "answer" a worked problem might show is never used; this app always computes its own.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/ocrService.ts` — `OCRService`, the single orchestration entry point (`recognizeText()`, `recognizeReceipt()`, `recognizeMath()`), each calling the resolved `OCRProvider` and, for the latter two, the matching parser. `getOCRService()` returns a shared, lazily-constructed instance, mirroring `src/lib/ai/aiService.ts`'s `getAIService()`.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/routeHelpers.ts` — `handleOCRRouteError()`/`statusForOCRErrorCode()`, shared `OCRProviderError` → HTTP response mapping used by all three new routes. Kept in `src/lib/ocr/` rather than re-exported from one `route.ts`, since a Next.js App Router route file may only export recognized route handlers (`GET`/`POST`/etc.) plus a small set of route-segment config values — any other export is invalid there.
- Created `src/lib/ocr/index.ts` — barrel export (`@/lib/ocr`) for everything above except `routeHelpers.ts` (imported directly by each route).
- Created `src/lib/ocr/README.md` — full architecture documentation (pieces table, setup/extension steps, security notes, and an explicit "out of scope" section naming the no-vendor-API constraint), mirroring `src/lib/ai/README.md`'s structure and depth.
- Created `src/app/api/ocr/image-to-text/route.ts` — `POST /api/ocr/image-to-text`: validates the request body/image, checks `isOCRConfigured()`, calls `getOCRService().recognizeText()`, returns `{ text, confidence?, provider }` or a typed `{ error, code }` (`503`/`not_configured` today, since no provider is connected).
- Created `src/app/api/ocr/receipt/route.ts` — `POST /api/ocr/receipt`: same shape, calls `recognizeReceipt()`, returns the structured receipt fields (`merchant`/`date`/`items`/`subtotal`/`tax`/`total`/`currency`) plus `rawText`.
- Created `src/app/api/ocr/math/route.ts` — `POST /api/ocr/math`: calls `recognizeMath()` to get a candidate expression, then — the same rule Task 30's `/api/ai/calculate` route already applies to the AI's own `expression` field — always re-evaluates it with `src/lib/calculator.ts`'s own, completely unchanged `evaluateExpression`/`formatExpressionForDisplay`/`formatResult`, returning a clear `502`/`provider_error` (never a fabricated number) if no expression was found or the engine can't evaluate what was extracted.
- Updated `.env.example` — appended one new, clearly-labeled `--- OCR Service ---` section (`OCR_PROVIDER`/`OCR_MODEL`/`OCR_API_KEY`/`OCR_BASE_URL`, all left blank) after the existing `--- AI Providers ---` section, explicitly noting — unlike that section — that no vendor is implemented or connected here. Every existing line above it is untouched.
- Updated `.env` (the project's own working environment file, already present and git-ignored) — the same additive `--- OCR Service ---` section, for consistency with how `.env.example` mirrors `.env` throughout the rest of the file. No existing value in this file was changed.
- Deliberately did **not**: add any OCR UI (no button, panel, upload affordance, or webcam capture was added to `Calculator.tsx`, the topbar, or anywhere else — this task's instructions were to implement the architecture only); touch `src/lib/calculator.ts` (byte-for-byte unchanged — the math route only *calls* its existing exported `evaluateExpression`/`formatExpressionForDisplay`/`formatResult`, exactly like Task 30's AI Calculator route already does); touch anything under `src/lib/ai/` or `src/app/api/ai/` (the AI Chat and AI Calculator features are completely unaffected — this is a new, separate architecture, not a modification of the existing one); add any new npm dependency (`imageInput.ts`/`receiptParser.ts`/`mathParser.ts` are plain TypeScript string/regex logic — `package.json`/`package-lock.json`/`bun.lock` are byte-for-byte unchanged); or call, reference, or hardcode any third-party OCR vendor endpoint, SDK, or API key anywhere in this project — `providers/index.ts`'s registry has exactly one entry, and `providers/noopProvider.ts` never makes a network call.

Task ID: 33
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Full project audit — identify and safely fix TypeScript issues, ESLint issues, build warnings, dead code, unused imports, duplicate logic, accessibility issues, hydration issues, React warnings, performance issues, console warnings, memory leaks, and security issues, without adding features or changing behavior. Run `npx tsc --noEmit`, `npx eslint .`, `npm run build`. Verify, update worklog, return the complete updated ZIP.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-32) before touching anything. Confirmed via a full-tree diff that this task's own upload is exactly Task 32's own delivered ZIP (byte-for-byte), so this audit starts from a already-reviewed, already-clean baseline rather than an unknown one.
- This sandbox session again has `bash_tool` network egress fully disabled (`npm ping` → `403 Forbidden`, `npm install` fails on the very first tarball fetch), so `npx eslint .` and `npm run build` could not be run live — neither tool's dependencies exist without `node_modules`. Worked around this as thoroughly as possible with the globally available standalone `typescript@6.0.3` and targeted static analysis, documented below category by category.
- **TypeScript issues / unused imports / dead code** — the one category this session could check with real precision despite no `node_modules`: temporarily enabled `noUnusedLocals`/`noUnusedParameters` in a scratch copy of `tsconfig.json` (never committed to the project) and ran `tsc --noEmit` against the whole project. This flagged exactly three genuine, safely-fixable findings (everything else was the same missing-`node_modules`/`@types/*` noise every prior network-constrained session has documented and filtered):
  - **`src/hooks/useMultiDeviceSync.ts`** — `pushMemoryToCloud` (from `@/lib/supabase/memorySync`) and `pushSettingsToCloud` (from `@/lib/supabase/settingsSync`) were imported but never called anywhere in the file — confirmed by reading the file end-to-end: Calculator Memory and Theme/Settings are reconciled by last-write-wins (fetch + conditionally `setMemory`/`setSettings` locally), which, unlike History/Favorites' union-merge, never needs to push a value back to the cloud, so these two imports were dead from the day this hook was written (Task 24). Removed both from their import statements; `fetchCloudMemory`/`fetchCloudSettings` (which are used) are untouched, and the file's actual reconciliation logic — what it fetches, compares, and applies — was not touched in any way.
  - **`src/components/calculator/HistoryPanel.tsx`** — `handleNoteKey`'s second parameter, `id: string`, was declared but never read inside the function body (only `event.key`/`event.target` are used); its one call site (`onKeyDown={(e) => handleNoteKey(e, item.id)}`) passed `item.id` in purely because the parameter existed, not because the handler needed it. Removed the unused parameter and simplified the call site to `onKeyDown={handleNoteKey}` — behavior is identical (the handler still blurs the input on Enter), just without a value that was never consulted.
  - Re-ran the same `noUnusedLocals`/`noUnusedParameters` check after both fixes: zero remaining findings anywhere in the project.
- **React warnings / Hydration issues** — re-examined the one specific, already-documented finding on record from Task 31's own live `eslint` session: a `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` violation in `src/components/chat/ChatWindow.tsx`'s mount-time `localStorage`-restore effect (independently re-confirmed as still present and unmodified through Task 32). Concluded, on inspection, that the underlying pattern itself is correct and should not be restructured: `localStorage` doesn't exist during server rendering, so this "use client" component intentionally restores its saved conversation in a `useEffect` that only runs after mount/hydration completes, rather than in a `useState` lazy initializer — which would run during SSR too (returning an empty conversation there, since `window`/`localStorage` aren't available) and then again on the client's first render (returning the real saved conversation), producing an actual server/client mismatch. Converting this to a lazy initializer to satisfy the lint rule would trade a lint finding for a real hydration bug, which this task's own "fix only issues that can be safely resolved without changing behavior" instruction rules out. Instead, added two narrowly-scoped `// eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` comments (with an inline explanation) directly above the two `setState` calls this effect makes (`setMessages(restored)`, `setHistoryLoaded(true)`) — a comment-only change that cannot alter runtime behavior in any way, silences the specific known false positive at its exact source, and leaves every other line of this effect (and the rest of the file) untouched.
- **ESLint issues (general)** — reviewed `eslint.config.mjs`: this project has already deliberately turned off `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars`, `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps`, `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any`, and roughly a dozen other rules project-wide (a considered decision predating this task, not something to second-guess or re-enable here), so the realistic remaining surface for a genuine ESLint finding is narrow. Since `eslint` itself isn't runnable this session, treated the `noUnusedLocals`/`noUnusedParameters` `tsc` pass above as the closest available proxy for the disabled `no-unused-vars` rule (which is exactly the "unused imports"/"dead code" category this task separately calls out), and manually reasoned through the one already-known real `eslint`-only finding (`set-state-in-effect`, addressed above) rather than guessing at others without a way to verify them.
- **Console warnings** — grepped the entire `src/` tree for `console.log(`: zero matches outside test files. The 6 existing `console.warn`/`console.error` calls project-wide were each individually reviewed in context and are all intentional, already-scoped error/diagnostic logging (e.g. `src/lib/ocr/routeHelpers.ts`/`src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts`'s server-side `console.error` on a caught provider error) — none is a leftover debug statement.
- **Memory leaks** — reviewed every file that calls `setInterval`/`addEventListener` (16 files: hooks, sync stores, UI components). Spot-checked the ones most likely to leak (`useMultiDeviceSync.ts`'s polling interval + 3 window/document listeners, `useEscapeToClose.ts`, `use-mobile.ts`'s `useSyncExternalStore`-based media-query subscription, `useInstallPrompt.ts`'s `beforeinstallprompt`/`appinstalled` listeners) line by line: every one already returns a cleanup function from its `useEffect` (or, for `use-mobile.ts`, uses `useSyncExternalStore`, which React itself unsubscribes) that clears its interval/removes its own listener — no missing cleanup found anywhere; nothing changed.
- **Security issues** — grepped the whole project for `dangerouslySetInnerHTML` (one match, in the untouched, unused `src/components/ui/chart.tsx` shadcn/ui primitive — injects only developer-authored CSS custom-property strings from a typed `ChartConfig`, never user/network input, matching the standard shadcn/ui chart pattern shipped by the library itself), `eval(` (zero matches), `target="_blank"` (zero matches, so no missing-`rel="noopener noreferrer"` risk), and hardcoded secret-shaped strings (`api_key\s*[:=]\s*['"]...`, `sk-...`, `AIza...`) across `src/`, `.env`, and `.env.example` (zero matches — every credential slot in both env files remains blank, exactly as every AI/OCR task since Task 25 left it). No change needed.
- **Accessibility issues** — grepped every `<img>` and `<Image>` in `src/` for a missing `alt` attribute: zero matches (every image already has one). Spot-checked icon-only buttons and interactive elements already in the codebase (topbar buttons, panel close buttons, chat send button) for `aria-label`/`title` presence — all already labeled, consistent with every prior task's own accessibility-conscious pattern (documented repeatedly since early tasks). No change needed.
- **Duplicate logic** — reviewed the two areas most likely to have drifted duplicate implementations given the project's own history (two natural-language paths: the rule-based Smart Bar (`src/lib/nlp.ts`) vs. the AI Calculator (`src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts`), and two OCR/AI "recognizer proposes, engine computes" routes (`src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts` vs. `src/app/api/ocr/math/route.ts`)): confirmed these are intentionally parallel, not accidentally duplicated — each calls into the same single, shared `src/lib/calculator.ts` engine rather than reimplementing evaluation logic itself, exactly as Tasks 30/31 designed and documented. No genuine copy-pasted logic found to consolidate; left as-is, since deduplicating intentionally-parallel-but-independent feature entry points would be a refactor, not a bug fix.

Task ID: 34
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Production security audit — verify and improve Supabase RLS, authentication security, environment variables, API key protection, input validation, error handling, session handling, and cloud sync security, without changing existing features (Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, calculator features, AGC branding, PDF/export branding, favicon).

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-33) before touching anything. Confirmed this upload is Task 33's own delivered ZIP.
- Reviewed each requested area by direct source inspection:
  - **Supabase RLS** — read all nine migrations in `supabase/migrations/`. Every app table (`profiles`, `calculator_history`, `user_settings`, `calculator_memory`, `favorites`) already has `row level security` enabled with `select`/`insert`/`update` (and `delete` where appropriate) policies scoped to `auth.uid() = user_id` (or `= id` for `profiles`), `to authenticated` only. No table is missing RLS, no policy grants broader access than "own rows only", and the two auto-provisioning trigger functions (`handle_new_auth_user*`) are the only `security definer` functions, each narrowly scoped to inserting exactly one row for the new `auth.users` id — already the correct, minimal-privilege pattern. No RLS change was needed or made.
  - **Authentication security** — `src/lib/supabase/oauth.ts` uses Supabase's own redirect-based `signInWithOAuth` (Google/GitHub) exclusively; no password handling, no manually-managed token exchange, and `src/app/auth/callback/route.ts` performs `exchangeCodeForSession` server-side via the cookie-aware server client, never accepting or trusting a token from the client directly. `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` (the one credential that bypasses RLS) is read by exactly one function (`getSupabaseServiceRoleKey()` in `src/lib/supabase/env.ts`) and confirmed via project-wide grep to be called from *nowhere* — no route, hook, or component uses the service-role key today, so it cannot leak to the browser or be misused server-side even though the env slot exists for a future admin operation.
  - **Environment variables** — confirmed `.env`/`.env.example` ship with every credential blank (Supabase, AI, OCR) and `.gitignore` already excludes `.env*` while explicitly allowing `.env.example`. Confirmed every `NEXT_PUBLIC_`-prefixed variable is one Supabase already documents as safe to expose (project URL, anon key — access is enforced by RLS, not secrecy), and every genuinely secret variable (`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`, `AI_API_KEY`, `OPENAI_API_KEY`, `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `GEMINI_API_KEY`, `OCR_API_KEY`) is read only from `server-only`-guarded modules (`src/lib/supabase/env.ts`, `src/lib/ai/env.ts`, `src/lib/ocr/env.ts`). No secret is read from a `"use client"` file anywhere in the project (checked via grep across every client component).
  - **API key protection** — re-verified `src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts` and `src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts` never forward `error.cause` (which can carry a raw vendor response body) to the browser, only to server-side `console.error`; confirmed all three AI provider files (`openaiProvider.ts`/`claudeProvider.ts`/`geminiProvider.ts`) read their key from `process.env` server-side only and never include it in a logged or returned value. No key of any kind is hardcoded anywhere in `src/` (grep for `sk-`, `AIza`, `api_key\s*[:=]`: zero matches).
  - **Input validation** — every `/api/ai/*` and `/api/ocr/*` route already validates its body's shape/type before use (`typeof x !== "string"`, non-blank checks, length caps: 8000 chars for chat messages, 500 for AI Calculator queries) and `src/lib/ocr/imageInput.ts`'s `parseImageDataUrl()` already enforces an allow-list of three MIME types, a strict data-URL regex, and an 8,000,000-character cap before any image ever reaches a provider. This validation was already solid — nothing here needed correction.
  - **Error handling** — every API route already normalizes thrown errors into a typed `{ error, code }` JSON body with an appropriate HTTP status via a shared `statusForErrorCode`/`handleOCRRouteError` helper, and already avoids leaking raw provider/database error internals to the client. No change needed.
  - **Session handling** — `src/lib/auth/session.ts`/`src/app/api/auth/session/route.ts` are an intentionally inert placeholder (no cookie is ever issued by this project's own backend; real session state lives entirely in Supabase's own `@supabase/ssr` cookie, read via `src/lib/supabase/server.ts`). Found one genuine, safely-fixable gap here: `src/lib/auth/authStore.ts` (the local, `localStorage`-backed mirror `SessionProvider` reads for instant/offline-tolerant UI state) was persisting the full Supabase `access_token` (a live bearer JWT) into `localStorage` on every sign-in, even though nothing in the entire project (`grep -rn "session.token"` across `src/`) ever reads that field back out for an actual request — every authenticated Supabase call already goes through the Supabase browser/server client's own cookie-backed session, not this field. Persisting a live bearer token to disk-backed `localStorage` for no functional reason needlessly widens the blast radius of any future XSS or local-storage-reading code. Fixed by redacting `token` to `""` in the copy written to `localStorage` inside `persist()`, while the in-memory `cache` for the current tab/page-load keeps the real value unchanged — `isValidSession()`'s shape check, `AuthSession`'s type, and every consumer of `useAuth()`/`session` are completely untouched, since nothing ever read the token from the persisted copy in the first place. `SessionProvider`'s own mount-time `supabase.auth.getSession()` hydration (which reads the real, cookie-backed session) still runs exactly as before and repopulates the in-memory session correctly on every reload — verified by re-reading `SessionProvider.tsx` end to end after the change.
  - **Cloud sync security** — read `historySync.ts`/`favoritesSync.ts`/`memorySync.ts`/`settingsSync.ts` in full: every read/write already goes through the anon-key, cookie-authenticated Supabase client (never the service-role key) and is scoped to the caller's own `user_id`, so RLS is the actual enforcement boundary regardless of what a compromised client attempted to send — matches the "RLS enforces access, not client-side trust" model Supabase itself recommends. Guest-mode data never reaches these functions at all (`useHistorySync.ts` and its siblings only call the Supabase layer once `useAuth().isAuthenticated` is true), so Guest Mode's local-only storage is unaffected by any of this review.
- Found and fixed one additional, adjacent production-hardening gap while reviewing "API key protection"/"cloud sync security": the five unauthenticated API routes that either call a paid external AI/OCR vendor once configured, or do non-trivial server-side image/expression processing (`/api/ai/chat`, `/api/ai/calculate`, `/api/ocr/image-to-text`, `/api/ocr/receipt`, `/api/ocr/math`) had no per-client throttle — a single client (signed in or guest) could call any of them without limit. Added `src/lib/rateLimit.ts`, a small `server-only` module (`checkRateLimit`/`getClientIp`/`rateLimitedResponse`): a fixed-window, per-route, per-client-IP counter held in a module-level `Map` (with a size-based self-prune, so it can't grow unbounded over a long-running process), returning a standard `{ error, code: "rate_limited" }` 429 with a `Retry-After` header — the exact same response shape every route's existing error handling already produces for other failure modes, so no client-side special case is needed. Wired into each of the five routes as the very first check in their `POST` handler (20/minute for the two text-only AI routes, 10/minute for the three image-carrying OCR routes, which take a larger request body and — once a provider is configured — real per-call processing cost): a rejected request never reaches body parsing, `isAIConfigured()`/`isOCRConfigured()`, or any provider call. This is a single-process, in-memory limiter (not a distributed one — a multi-instance deployment would need a shared store such as Redis), documented as such in the module's own comment, but it costs no new dependency or environment variable and meaningfully raises the bar against casual single-client abuse of endpoints that, once configured, incur a real vendor bill.
- Added baseline HTTP security headers via `next.config.ts`'s `headers()` (a new, additive export — `typescript.ignoreBuildErrors`/`reactStrictMode` untouched): `X-Frame-Options: DENY` (clickjacking), `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff` (MIME-sniffing), `Referrer-Policy: strict-origin-when-cross-origin`, and `Permissions-Policy: camera=(), microphone=(), geolocation=()` (confirmed via project-wide grep that nothing in the app calls `getUserMedia`/geolocation — only `navigator.clipboard`, which this policy doesn't affect). Deliberately did **not** add a `Content-Security-Policy`: this app loads Google Fonts, calls external currency-rate APIs (`open.er-api.com`/`frankfurter.app`), and (once configured) reaches AI/OCR vendor APIs and renders PDF/export output — a generic CSP risks silently breaking one of those already-working features, which this task's own instructions rule out trading for a hardening change. Every header added here only removes behavior (framing, sniffing, referrer leakage, camera/mic/geolocation access) the app never relied on.
- Verified the fixes don't regress anything:
  - Ran a full parse-level syntax check (TypeScript compiler's own `createSourceFile`, bypassing module resolution) on every file touched this session (`src/lib/rateLimit.ts`, all five modified API routes, `src/lib/auth/authStore.ts`, `next.config.ts`): zero parse errors.
  - Ran `npx tsc --noEmit -p tsconfig.json` (globally available `typescript@6.0.3`, no project `node_modules` — this sandbox session again has `bash_tool` network egress fully disabled, confirmed via `npm ping` → `403 Forbidden`, so a live `next build`/`npm install`/project-aware `tsc` round-trip was not possible, consistent with every prior network-constrained session): every diagnostic touching a file this session modified is the same standing "missing `node_modules`" noise every prior session has documented (`Cannot find module 'next/server'`/`'server-only'` etc.) — zero real type errors introduced by this session's changes.
  - Diffed the entire project tree against the received upload (`diff -rq`, excluding `node_modules`/`.next`/`worklog.md`): confirmed exactly **eight files changed**, all as described above — `next.config.ts`, `src/app/api/ai/chat/route.ts`, `src/app/api/ai/calculate/route.ts`, `src/app/api/ocr/image-to-text/route.ts`, `src/app/api/ocr/receipt/route.ts`, `src/app/api/ocr/math/route.ts`, `src/lib/auth/authStore.ts` — plus one new file, `src/lib/rateLimit.ts`. Nothing else in the project — every calculator/converter/history/memory/settings/favorites/about/account/profile component, all Supabase RLS policies/migrations, all six history export formats, AGC branding/PDF exports/favicon, Guest Mode, Google Login, GitHub Login, and the entire AI Chat/AI Calculator/OCR feature set — was touched. `package.json`/lockfiles/`.env`/`.env.example`/`eslint.config.mjs`/`tsconfig.json`/`supabase/migrations/*` are all byte-for-byte unchanged — no dependency, environment variable, or database schema was added, removed, or altered.
  - Removed the scratch `tsconfig.tsbuildinfo` incremental-build-cache file this session's own analysis produced before packaging (never part of the deliverable, same packaging hygiene every prior task follows).

Stage Summary:
- Audited all eight requested areas (Supabase RLS, authentication security, environment variables, API key protection, input validation, error handling, session handling, cloud sync security) and found the project already in strong shape across most of them — RLS, input validation, error handling, and API-key handling in particular were already production-grade from prior tasks and needed no change.
- Made three real, narrowly-scoped, additive security improvements: (1) stopped persisting the live Supabase bearer token to `localStorage` in `authStore.ts` (redacted on write, kept in-memory for the current tab — nothing ever read the persisted copy, so this is a pure exposure reduction with zero behavior change); (2) added a lightweight per-IP rate limiter (`src/lib/rateLimit.ts`) to the five unauthenticated AI/OCR API routes, closing an abuse/cost-DoS gap against endpoints that call paid external vendors once configured; (3) added baseline HTTP security headers (`X-Frame-Options`, `X-Content-Type-Options`, `Referrer-Policy`, `Permissions-Policy`) via `next.config.ts`, deliberately stopping short of a `Content-Security-Policy` to avoid any risk to this app's existing fonts/currency/AI/OCR/PDF features.
- Confirmed no existing functionality was broken: Guest Mode, Google Login, and GitHub Login are untouched at the architecture level (`src/lib/auth/routes.ts`, `src/contexts/auth-context.ts`, `src/components/auth/SessionProvider.tsx`, `src/lib/supabase/{client,server,oauth,mapUser}.ts`, `src/app/auth/callback/route.ts` are all byte-for-byte unchanged); every calculator/converter feature, AGC branding, PDF/export branding, and the favicon are untouched; every Supabase RLS policy and migration is untouched; and a full-tree diff against the received upload confirms exactly eight files changed plus one new file, with `package.json`, lockfiles, `.env`/`.env.example`, `eslint.config.mjs`, `tsconfig.json`, and `supabase/migrations/*` all byte-for-byte identical to the upload. `npx tsc --noEmit` and a full parse-level syntax check on every touched file show zero errors introduced by this session; `npm install`/`next build`/`npx eslint .` could not be run live due to this sandbox's fully disabled network egress this session, consistent with every prior constrained session, and is recorded here plainly rather than glossed over.

Task ID: 35
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: Performance/bundle optimization pass — bundle size, lazy loading, dynamic imports, React rendering, memoization, image/CSS optimization — without changing any feature, the AGC branding, PDF/export branding, favicon, calculator features, Guest Mode, Google Login, or GitHub Login.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-34) before touching anything, confirmed this upload is Task 34's own delivered ZIP (byte-for-byte via `diff -rq`), and read every file this task plausibly touches (`src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx` and every component it renders, `src/app/layout.tsx`, `src/app/page.tsx`, `next.config.ts`, `package.json`) before making changes.
- This sandbox session again has `bash_tool` network egress fully disabled (`npm ping` → `403 Forbidden`), so `npm install`/`npx eslint .`/`npm run build`/a real bundle-analyzer run were not possible — consistent with every prior network-constrained session (Tasks 3/4/7A/29/31/33/34). Worked from direct source inspection plus the globally available standalone `typescript@6.0.3` for verification, documented below.

**Bundle size / lazy loading / dynamic imports (the main win this session):**
- Audited `Calculator.tsx` (the component every page load renders) and found nine child components imported statically even though none of them can be visible on first paint of the default Standard-mode calculator: `HistoryPanel` (511 lines), `Converter` (279), `AICalculatorPanel` (264), `AccountPanel` (219), `HistoryPanel`'s siblings `FavoritesPanel` (204), `SettingsPanel` (191), `SmartBar` (103), `AboutPanel` (98), and `ScientificKeypad` (39) — six of these are slide-out panels that start `open={false}`, and the other three (`Converter`, `SmartBar`, `ScientificKeypad`) only render once the user switches away from the default Standard mode / opens the Smart input bar. All nine were being bundled into the same initial JS chunk as the calculator itself for zero first-paint benefit.
- Rewrote the import section of `Calculator.tsx`: replaced all nine static `import { X } from "./X"` lines with `next/dynamic` code-split imports (`dynamic(() => import("./X").then((m) => m.X), { ssr: false })`), each with a comment explaining why `ssr: false` is safe here (every one of these is already a `"use client"` component that renders nothing, or a fixed/absolute-positioned overlay, when closed — no server-rendered layout to reserve, no hydration-mismatch risk). `Display`, `Keypad`, `MemoryBar`, `ModeTabs`, and `InstallBanner` — the parts of the UI actually visible on first paint — were deliberately left as ordinary static imports; only genuinely deferrable code was touched. The exported component name/API of every one of the nine untouched target files (`HistoryPanel.tsx`, `FavoritesPanel.tsx`, etc.) was not changed — this is purely a call-site change in the one file that imports them.
- Net effect: the initial `/` page's JS bundle no longer needs to include History/Favorites/Settings/About/Account/AI-Calculator panel code, the Converter (currency+units, including `CurrencySelect`), the Smart input bar, or the Scientific keypad until the user actually opens/switches to one of them — each becomes its own on-demand chunk fetched at that point, exactly the "lazy loading" / "dynamic imports" / "bundle size" outcome this task asked for, with no change to what any of them render or how they behave once loaded.

**React rendering / memoization:**
- Audited every component under `src/components/calculator/` for `React.memo` usage (found none anywhere in the project) and for which ones receive props that are stable or change far less often than their parent (`Calculator`) re-renders — `Calculator` re-renders on effectively every keystroke, since `useCalculator()`'s returned `calc` object is a fresh object literal each render (deliberately — its own state, e.g. the live expression/result, genuinely does change on nearly every interaction, so memoizing `Keypad`/`Display`/`MemoryBar`/`ScientificKeypad`, which all consume `calc` directly, would add a comparison cost with no real re-render savings and was correctly left alone rather than wrapped for the sake of it).
- Found two components whose *own* props are effectively stable across `Calculator`'s frequent re-renders and wrapped both in `React.memo`:
  - `ModeTabs.tsx` — its only props are `mode` (only changes when the user actually switches Standard/Scientific/Converter) and `onChange` (`calc.setMode`, a React `useState` setter — a stable function identity even though the `calc` object wrapping it is new every render). Renamed the existing function to `ModeTabsImpl` and exported `export const ModeTabs = memo(ModeTabsImpl)`, so every call site (`Calculator.tsx`, unchanged) keeps importing/using `ModeTabs` exactly as before.
  - `InstallBanner.tsx` — takes **zero** props (all its state comes from its own `useInstallPrompt()` hook). Memoizing it means `Calculator`'s per-keystroke re-renders never re-render this subtree at all; it only re-renders when its own hook's state actually changes (i.e. exactly when `canInstall` flips). Same rename-to-`Impl`-plus-memo-export pattern, same unchanged call site.
- Did not add memoization to `CalculatorButton`/`Keypad`'s 20 button instances: `Keypad.tsx` builds each button's `onClick` as an inline arrow (`() => inputDigit("7")`), a fresh function reference every render, so wrapping `CalculatorButton` in `memo` would compare-and-still-re-render every time — no real gain, and restructuring `useCalculator`'s action signatures or `Keypad`'s callback wiring to make those props stable would be a genuine behavior-risking refactor of core calculator logic, outside this task's "preserve functionality, change only required files, no unrelated refactoring" constraints. Left untouched.
- Stabilized `Calculator.tsx`'s own `handleReuse` callback (passed down to the now-lazy `HistoryPanel`/`FavoritesPanel`) with `useCallback` keyed on `calc.loadResult` (itself a stable function from `useCalculator`'s internal `useReducer`-backed dispatch) instead of being redefined as a new closure on every render — a small, safe reference-stability improvement with no behavior change (same three statements run in the same order on every call).

**Image optimization:**
- Audited every `<Image>` usage in the project (`page.tsx`, `SplashScreen.tsx`, `InstallBanner.tsx`, `AboutPanel.tsx`, `SettingsPanel.tsx`, `AccountPanel.tsx`, `ProfileView.tsx`): all already use `next/image` (zero raw `<img>` tags anywhere in `src/`), all already pass explicit `width`/`height` matched to their actual rendered size (26–96px marks/avatars, no oversized source being downscaled by CSS), `priority` is already only set on the two above-the-fold marks that need it (splash screen, page header), and the two remote/user-supplied avatar images (`AccountPanel.tsx`, `ProfileView.tsx`) are already correctly marked `unoptimized` (they're OAuth-provider/base64 avatar URLs, not project assets `next/image`'s built-in optimizer can process). Concluded this was already in a good state from prior tasks — no change needed, and no PNG asset was re-encoded or resized (this sandbox has no `sharp`/Pillow-with-network available this session, and re-touching any AGC brand asset risks the "keep AGC branding... unchanged unless required" constraint for zero measurable benefit given the audit above).

**CSS optimization:**
- Reviewed `src/app/globals.css` (3,699 lines, Tailwind v4 + a large hand-written `--c-*`-token-based theme layer accumulated additively across Tasks 1-33). Confirmed styling is already Tailwind v4's JIT engine (only classes actually referenced in the codebase are ever emitted — no manual purge step needed or missing) plus one global stylesheet of hand-authored rules that are already selector-scoped per component (`.calc-history-*`, `.calc-csel-*`, etc.) rather than duplicated. Splitting this single file into per-component CSS modules would be a structural rewrite touching dozens of components' className wiring for a framework (Next.js/Tailwind) that already ships it as one minified/gzipped stylesheet either way — real risk of visual regression across the four themes for no verifiable bundle-size win in a sandbox that can't run a build to measure one, so this was intentionally left as pure audit with no changes, consistent with "no unrelated refactoring or reorganization."

**Font loading (small additive fix found while auditing render-blocking resources):**
- `src/app/layout.tsx` loads three Google Fonts via `next/font/google` (`Geist`, `Geist_Mono`, `Space_Grotesk`). Noticed `Space_Grotesk` already specifies `display: "swap"` (added in Phase 1) but `Geist`/`Geist_Mono` did not — meaning, on a slow connection, body text in those two fonts could stay invisible (FOIT) until the webfont finishes loading instead of rendering immediately in a fallback font and swapping in. Added `display: "swap"` to both, matching the treatment `Space_Grotesk` already had. Purely additive font-loading-strategy config — no font family, weight, subset, or CSS variable name changed, so every existing `font-sans`/`font-mono`/`font-display` usage across the app is visually identical once the fonts load; the only observable difference is that text no longer stays invisible while they load.

**Audited and confirmed already optimal (no change needed):**
- Grepped for every heavy dependency in `package.json` that a generic Next.js/shadcn scaffold often carries but this app may not actually use (`react-markdown`, `react-syntax-highlighter`, `recharts`, `embla-carousel-react`, `@dnd-kit/*`, `next-auth`, `next-intl`, `@mdxeditor/editor`, `react-day-picker`, `input-otp`, `vaul`, `cmdk`): confirmed every one of them is referenced only inside unused `src/components/ui/*` shadcn primitives (`chart.tsx`, `carousel.tsx`, `calendar.tsx`, `command.tsx`, `drawer.tsx`, `sidebar.tsx`, `form.tsx`, `input-otp.tsx`) that are themselves never imported from anywhere reachable in the app (`grep -rl "components/ui/chart"` etc. across `src/` returns nothing outside the file itself) — so none of this weight is actually included in any real page's bundle today; there was nothing to lazy-load or remove.
- `src/lib/exportHistory.ts`'s heavy export-format libraries (`jspdf`, `exceljs`, `docx`/SheetJS-equivalent) were already dynamically imported inside their respective `exportHistory*` functions since Task 3/5 (`await import("jspdf")`, `await import("exceljs")`, `await import("docx")`) — already correct lazy-loading, not touched.
- The `/chat` and `/profile` routes are separate Next.js pages (`src/app/chat/page.tsx`, `src/app/profile/page.tsx`), so the framework's own route-based code-splitting already keeps their JS (including `ChatWindow`/`MessageList`/`ChatMessageBubble`, none of which pull in `react-markdown`/`react-syntax-highlighter` despite those packages being in `package.json`) out of the home page's bundle with zero action needed here.
- Reviewed every `setInterval`/`addEventListener` hook (`useMultiDeviceSync.ts`, `useEscapeToClose.ts`, `use-mobile.ts`, `useInstallPrompt.ts`) for the "React rendering" angle (unnecessary re-render-triggering state updates) — all already gate their state writes behind actual value changes (e.g. `use-mobile.ts` via `useSyncExternalStore`), consistent with Task 33's own memory-leak audit of the same files; no redundant re-render sources found.

Stage Summary:

Task ID: 36
Agent: Claude (chat)
Task: PWA review — Service Worker, Offline Mode, Install Prompt, Manifest, Icons, Splash Screens, Background Sync. Fix verified production issues only.

Work Log:
- Read `worklog.md` in full (Tasks 1-35) before touching anything. No new ZIP was uploaded for this task, so continued from this session's own most-recently-delivered state (Task 35's output, itself Task 34's ZIP plus Task 35's bundle-optimization changes) rather than re-starting from the older Task 34 upload still sitting in the uploads folder.
- Reviewed each requested PWA area by direct source inspection (this sandbox again has `bash_tool` network egress fully disabled — `npm ping` → `403 Forbidden` — so no live `next build`/Lighthouse/browser run was possible; verification below is static-analysis-based, consistent with most prior sessions):
  - **Service Worker (`public/sw.js`)** — found one real, verified production bug: the `fetch` handler's "static assets: cache-first" branch intercepted *every* same-origin `GET` request that wasn't a navigation, with no distinction between actual static sub-resources and plain `fetch()`/XHR calls. Two concrete consequences: (1) `GET /api/currency` (which already has its own correct 1-hour TTL + primary/fallback/offline rate chain server-side, from Tasks 3/4) would be cached by the service worker on its first successful response and then served from that cache forever afterwards — this cache has no expiry logic — permanently freezing exchange rates regardless of the route's own freshness logic; (2) `GET /api/auth/session` (which `SessionProvider` calls on mount to reconcile Google/GitHub sign-in state per Task 25's architecture) would likewise be frozen at whatever it first returned, risking a client that never sees a real sign-in reflected after the SW has cached one "signed out" response — a direct risk to the explicitly-protected Google Login/GitHub Login features. A third, related risk: Next.js App Router's own RSC data fetches for client-side navigation (`next/link` transitions) reuse a page's URL but return a different, non-HTML payload than a full navigation to that same URL — both have an empty `request.destination` (unlike a real script/style/image/font/manifest fetch) but would have been cached under the same cache key by the old blanket branch, risking the wrong payload type being served back later for that URL.
  - **Fix**: added a single guard, `if (!request.destination) return;`, right before the cache-first branch — real static sub-resources (scripts, styles, images, fonts, the manifest) all have a non-empty `destination` and are completely unaffected; same-origin API routes and RSC data fetches (empty `destination`) now always reach the network untouched, exactly as they would with no service worker installed at all. Bumped `CACHE` from `"agc-calc-v2"` to `"agc-calc-v3"` so any already-cached stale entries for these paths (from before this fix) are simply never read again (the `activate` handler's existing cleanup deletes any cache key that isn't the current one). No other line of `sw.js` — the app-shell precache list, the install/activate lifecycle, the navigation network-first-with-offline-fallback strategy, or the static-asset cache-first strategy itself — was changed.
  - **Offline Mode** — re-verified the navigation fallback chain (`network-first → caches.match(request) → caches.match("/")`) is otherwise sound: a direct offline visit to a previously-uncached route falls back to the cached app shell at `"/"`, which is the calculator's own client-side logic (not a generic "you're offline" placeholder) and remains fully functional offline — confirmed this is intentional/correct behavior, not a bug, and left unchanged. The currency converter's own three-tier offline fallback (`primary → frankfurter → static offline table`, Task 4) and its `source: "offline"` UI badge are untouched and, if anything, are now more correct with the service-worker fix above (they can no longer be masked by a frozen SW-cached response sitting in front of the route).
  - **Install Prompt (`src/hooks/useInstallPrompt.ts`, `InstallBanner.tsx`)** — re-read end to end: `beforeinstallprompt` is correctly captured with `preventDefault()` and deferred, `appinstalled` correctly clears the deferred prompt and flips `installed`, the already-installed check via `display-mode: standalone` (plus iOS's `navigator.standalone`) runs before first paint via a `useState` initializer, and the dismiss flag is persisted to `localStorage` and correctly gates `canInstall`. No verified bug found — left unchanged.
  - **Manifest (`public/manifest.json`)** — re-checked every field: `start_url`/`scope` both `"/"` (matches `next.config.ts`, which has no `basePath`), `display: "standalone"`, `background_color`/`theme_color` both `#0a0e17` (matches `layout.tsx`'s `viewport.themeColor`, so no white/mismatched-color flash on launch), a full icon set from 72px to 512px all with `purpose: "any"`, plus separate dedicated `icon-maskable-192`/`icon-maskable-512` entries with `purpose: "maskable"` (correctly *not* combined as `"any maskable"` on the same entry, which is the discouraged pattern — a maskable icon needs its own safe-zone-padded artwork, which these already have per Task 7A's icon generation). No verified bug found — left unchanged.
  - **Icons** — cross-checked every icon path referenced by `manifest.json` and `layout.tsx`'s `<head>` (`favicon.ico`, `icon-16/32/48/72/96/128/144/152/180/192/384/512.png`, `icon-maskable-192/512.png`, `apple-touch-icon.png` + `-152`/`-167` variants, `mask-icon.svg`) against the actual files in `public/`: every referenced file exists, no broken links. No verified bug found — left unchanged.
  - **Splash Screens** — cross-checked every `apple-touch-startup-image` `media` query in `layout.tsx` (9 entries) against the actual device-pixel dimensions they claim (e.g. `750×1334` @ 375×667 CSS px / 2x ≈ iPhone SE/8, `1170×2532` @ 390×844 CSS px / 3x ≈ iPhone 12/13/14, `1620×2160` @ 810×1080 CSS px / 2x ≈ iPad 10.2", `2048×2732` @ 1024×1366 CSS px / 2x ≈ iPad Pro 12.9") and confirmed every one of the 9 pairings is a correct, standard Apple splash-screen size/media-query match, and every referenced `splash-*.png` file exists in `public/`. No verified bug found — left unchanged.
  - **Background Sync** — grepped the entire project for the Background Sync API (`registration.sync`, `periodicSync`, `sync.register`, a `self.addEventListener("sync", ...)` handler in `sw.js`): zero usage anywhere. This isn't a defect to fix — the app was never built against that API, and implementing it fresh would be a new feature, not a fix, which this task's own "fix verified production issues only" / "no unrelated... redesign" instructions rule out. Noted for completeness: the app already has an equivalent *application-level* reconnect behavior (`useMultiDeviceSync.ts`'s `window.addEventListener("online", ...)` triggering an immediate re-check/re-sync of history/favorites/settings/memory against Supabase — Task 24), which covers the practical "pick back up after being offline" need without the Background Sync API; this was reviewed and confirmed already-correct, not touched.
- **Service worker update delivery (found while reviewing "Service Worker" holistically, not one of the seven bullet areas by name but directly about how promptly a service-worker fix like the one above actually reaches users):** a browser's update check for an installed service worker is a byte-for-byte re-fetch of the exact `sw.js` URL; if that response is ever served with a cacheable `Cache-Control` (by a CDN/edge in front of the deployment, since neither `next.config.ts` nor Next's own static-file serving set one explicitly before this task), that re-fetch can itself return a stale cached copy, silently delaying this task's own fix (and any future one) from reaching already-installed users indefinitely. Added a second `headers()` entry in `next.config.ts` scoped to `source: "/sw.js"` setting `Cache-Control: no-cache, must-revalidate` — forces every update check to revalidate with the origin instead of trusting an intermediary cache. This is additive (a new array entry alongside Task 34's existing `/:path*` security-header block, which is untouched) and doesn't change any response's content, only how promptly the browser notices when `sw.js` itself changes.

Verification & Fixes:
- Ran a Node `Function()` construction check on `public/sw.js` (plain-JS syntax validation, since it isn't part of the TypeScript project) — parses cleanly.
- Ran a full parse-level syntax check (TypeScript compiler's own `createSourceFile`) on `next.config.ts` and across all project `.ts`/`.tsx` files after this session's edits: zero parse errors anywhere.
- Manually re-traced `sw.js`'s new guard against every real request type the app makes: navigations (`mode === "navigate"`, handled by the untouched earlier branch, still network-first-with-offline-fallback) → unaffected; `_next/static/*` JS/CSS chunks, `next/image`-served images, `next/font` font files, and the `/manifest.json` fetch the browser itself makes (all have a non-empty `destination` — `"script"`, `"style"`, `"image"`, `"font"`, `"manifest"` respectively) → still cache-first as before, zero behavior change; `GET /api/currency` and `GET /api/auth/session` (empty `destination`) → now always reach the network, matching every other same-origin `fetch()`-based API call in the app (which were already bypassing the SW correctly whenever the browser happens to report a non-`""` destination inconsistently, or simply relying on the app's own logic — this fix makes that consistent and explicit rather than accidental).
- Diffed the entire project tree against this session's own starting point (`diff -rq`, excluding `node_modules`/`.next`/`worklog.md`): confirmed exactly **two additional files changed** this task — `public/sw.js` (cache-name bump + the one-line `destination` guard) and `next.config.ts` (one additive `headers()` entry for `/sw.js`) — on top of the four files Task 35 had already changed (`src/app/layout.tsx`, `src/components/calculator/Calculator.tsx`, `ModeTabs.tsx`, `InstallBanner.tsx`), for six total changed files relative to the original Task 34 upload. Nothing else in the project — `public/manifest.json`, every icon/splash-screen asset, `src/hooks/useInstallPrompt.ts`, `src/components/calculator/InstallBanner.tsx`'s own JSX/behavior (only its Task 35 `memo` wrapper carries over, untouched further here), the currency route's own caching/fallback logic, Supabase auth/session logic, AGC branding, PDF/export branding, the favicon, Guest Mode, and every calculator feature — was touched.

Stage Summary:
- Reviewed all seven requested PWA areas end to end.
